Effects of Reclamation (Istihqaq) in Sulh
Details the consequences of reclamation (istihqaq) in sulh contracts and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of istihqaq on a sulh contract and distinguish the relied-upon Hanafi position from the alternative narration.

Core Idea
Reclamation in sulh does not void the contract; it only requires proportional return of the consideration.

This passage from the Book of Sulh addresses a critical practical issue: what happens when the property or consideration in a settlement contract is later claimed by a third party? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer that preserves the settlement's finality while ensuring fairness. You will learn the general rule, its exceptions, and the intra-Hanafi dispute that shapes the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of reclamation
The passage distinguishes between reclamation of the subject matter (musalih 'anhu) and reclamation of the consideration (badal). Recognize that each triggers a different proportional return.
This is the foundational distinction for the entire ruling.
2
State the general rule of proportional return
When the subject matter is reclaimed, the defendant returns a proportionate part of the consideration. When the consideration is reclaimed, the claimant returns a proportionate part of the subject matter.
This ensures no party gains unjustly from the reclamation.
3
Examine the exception for sulh on benefits
When sulh involves a benefit (e.g., service, usufruct), it is treated as ijarah, requiring specification of time and voiding upon death of a party. Reclamation leads to proportional adjustment for the remaining benefit.
This exception is crucial because the contract type changes: it is a rent contract, not a sale.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad narrates from Abu Hanifa that reclamation of the consideration voids the sulh. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that it does not void; the claimant returns the like and the sulh stands. Determine the mufta bihi.
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
5
Apply the rule to a concrete example
Take the example of a claimant claiming 1000 dirhams and settling for 100. If the 100 is reclaimed, under the mufta bihi position, the claimant returns 100 and the sulh remains valid; the original claim is not revived.
This example illustrates the practical effect: the settlement stands despite reclamation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلح
عنه فإن استحق بعض المصالح عنه أو كله البدل لا جهالة المصالح المدعى عليه رجع بحصة ذلك عن العوض أو بكله ولو استحق المصالح عليه أو بعضه رجع بكل المصالح عنه أو ببعضه وإن وقع من مال بمنفعة اعتبر إجارة فيشترط التوقيت ويبطل بموت أحدهما والصلح عن سكوت أو إنكار فداء لليمين في حق المنكر ومعاوضة في حق المدعي فلا شفعة إن صالح عن داريهما وتجب لو صالح على داريهما ولو استحق المتنازع فيه رجع المدعي بالخصومة ورد البدل ولو بعضه فبقدره ولو استحق المصالح
الثانية إذا تصادقا على أن لا دين بطل الصلح كما لو استوفى عين حقه ثم تصادقا أن لا دين، فلو تصادقا على أن لا دين لا يبطل الشراء، وإن وقع على جنسه فإن كان بأقل من المدعي فهو حط وإبراء، وإن كان بمثله فهو قبض واستيفاء، وإن كان بأكثر فهو ربا، وإذا اعتبر بيعاً ثبتت أحكامه فيثبت به الشفعة والرد بالعيب وخيار الرؤية ويفسده جهالة الأجل والبدل) إن كان مما يحتاج إلى التسليم وإن استحق بعض المصالح عنه أو كله رجع المدعى عليه بحصة ذلك من العوض أو كله ولو استحق المصالح عليه أو بعضه رجع بكل المصالح عنه أو ببعضه وإن وقع عن مال بمنفعة اعتبر إجارة فثبت أحكامها فيشترط التوقيت) فيما يحتاج إليه كخدمة العبد وسكنى الدار بخلاف صبغ الثوب وركوب الدابة وحمل الطعام فالشرط بيان تلك المنفعة ( وتبطل بموت أحدهما إن عقدها لنفسه، وكذا بفوات المحل قبل الاستيفاء، ولو كان بعد استيفاء البعض بطل فيما بقي ويرجع بالمدعي بقدره ولو كان الصلح على خدمة عبد فقتل إن كان القاتل المولى بطل وإلا ضمن قيمته واشترى بها عبداً يخدمه إن شاء كالموصى بخدمته بخلاف المرهون حيث يضمن المولى بالإتلاف والعتق . وإنما يعتبر إجارة إذا وقع على خلاف المدعى به، فإن ادعى داراً فصالحه على سكناها شهراً فهو استيفاء لبعض حقه لا إجارة فتصح إجارته للمدعى عليه والصلح عن سكوت وإنكار فداء في حق المنكر ومعاوضة في حق المدعي) فبطل الصلح على دراهم بعد دعوى دراهم إذا تفرقا قبل القبض (فلا شفعة إن صالحا عن داريهما ويجب لو صالحا على داريهما ولا يحل للمدعي ما أخذه إن كان كاذباً ولا يبرأ المدعى عليه كذلك مما عليه وإن برئ قضاء إلا إذا أبرأه المدعي عما بقي (ولو استحق المتنازع فيه رجع المدعي بالخصومة) المستحق (ورد البدل ولو بعضه فبقدره ولو استحق المصالح مع عليه أو بعضه رجع إلى الدعوى في كله أو بعضه إلا إذا كان مما لا يتعين بالتعيين وهو من جنس المدعى به فحينئذ يرجع بمثل ما استحق ولا يبطل الصلح كما إذا ادعى ألفاً فصالحه على مائة وقبضها فإنه يرجع عليه بمائة عند استحقاقها، سواء كان الصلح بعد الإقرار أو المنح عن السراجية وحكى القولين في القنية قال الحموي في حاشية الأشباه : ما مشى عليه في الأشباه رواية محمد عن أبي حنيفة وما مشى عليه في البحر قولهما وهو الصحيح كما في معين المفتي
عليه أو بعضه رجع إلى الدعوى في كله أو بعضه وهلاك بدل الصلح قبل التسليم كاستحقاقه في الفصلين .
Book of Sulh. If part or all of the subject matter is reclaimed, the defendant returns a proportionate part of the consideration or all of it. If the consideration is reclaimed or part of it, he returns all or part of the subject matter. If the sulh is for property in exchange for a benefit, it is considered an ijarah, so timing is stipulated and it is voided by the death of either party. Sulh in case of silence or denial is a ransom for the oath regarding the denier and a transaction regarding the claimant, so there is no pre-emption if they make sulh concerning their two houses, but it is obligatory if they make sulh on their two houses. If the disputed property is reclaimed, the claimant returns to the claim and returns the consideration, or part of it proportionally. If what was given in sulh is reclaimed or part of it, he returns to the claim in whole or part, unless it is something non-specific and of the same genus as the claimed item, then he returns the like of what was reclaimed and the sulh is not voided, as if he claimed a thousand and made sulh for a hundred and took possession, then he returns a hundred when it is reclaimed, whether after acknowledgment or denial. The two opinions are narrated in al-Qunyah. Al-Hamawi said in Hashiyat al-Ashbah: what is followed in al-Ashbah is the narration of Muhammad from Abu Hanifa, and what is followed in al-Bahr is their opinion, which is the correct one as in Mu'in al-Mufti. If part or all of the subject matter is reclaimed, he returns to the claim in whole or part. The destruction of the sulh consideration before delivery is like its reclamation in the two sections.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage, from the Book of Sulh, is a ruling-with-proof section detailing the effects of reclamation (istihqaq) in a sulh contract. The author begins by stating a general rule: if part or all of the subject matter (musalih 'anhu) is reclaimed, the defendant (musalih 'alayhi) returns a proportionate part of the consideration (badal) or all of it. Conversely, if the consideration is reclaimed, the defendant returns part or all of the subject matter. This principle ensures that neither party gains unjustly. The passage then covers specific scenarios: when sulh involves a property for a benefit, it is treated as an ijarah contract, requiring specification of time and voiding upon death of either party. Sulh in cases of silence or denial is considered a ransom for the oath (for the denier) and a transaction (for the claimant). The author then discusses the effect of reclaiming the disputed property: the claimant returns to the original claim and returns the consideration (or part of it). However, if the sulh consideration is from the same genus as the claimed item and is non-specific (e.g., money), then upon reclamation, the claimant returns the like of it, and the sulh remains valid. An example is given: if someone claimed 1000 dirhams and settled for 100, then the 100 is reclaimed, he returns 100 and the sulh is not voided. The passage also mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad's narration from Abu Hanifa holds that the reclamation voids the sulh, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold it does not void. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The passage concludes by equating the destruction of the sulh consideration before delivery with its reclamation, applying the same rulings.

Key Terms
استحقاق (istihqaq): Reclamation of property from a party by a third party with a superior right.
المصالح عنه (al-musalih 'anhu): The subject matter of the sulh contract, i.e., the property or right being settled over.
البدل (al-badal): The consideration given in exchange for the subject matter in a sulh contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sulh contract, if the consideration given by the defendant is later reclaimed by a third party, what is the effect under the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) The sulh becomes void entirely.
B) The claimant returns the subject matter and the sulh is rescinded.
C) The claimant returns the like of the consideration, and the sulh remains valid.
D) The defendant must give a new consideration.

Key Takeaway
In a sulh contract, reclamation (istihqaq) does not invalidate the contract but requires proportional return of the consideration, following the Sahibayn's position.

General Permissibility and Exceptions in Sulh
States general permissibility and three exceptions with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on the permissibility of sulh over property, benefits, and crimes, and identify the three exceptions (hadd, marriage, slavery) along with the relevant conditions.

Core Idea
Sulh is permissible over property, benefits, and crimes, but never over fixed punishments, marriage, or slavery.

Sulh (settlement) is a flexible contract in Hanafi fiqh that can resolve disputes over most claims. However, certain rights are considered inviolable—such as Allah's prescribed punishments (hudud) and the sacred bonds of marriage and slavery—and cannot be compromised. This lesson anchors the general rule and its exceptions, plus key conditions when the sulh consideration is defective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Locate the opening statement: 'الصلح جائز عن دعوى المال والمنفعة والجناية'. This tells you sulh is valid over property, benefits, and crimes (jinaya, i.e., intentional torts or qisas).
This is a broad permission; all three categories involve private rights that can be waived or compromised.
2
Recognize the exceptions
After the general rule, note the phrase 'بخلاف الحد ومن النكاح والرق قبله'. Committed sulh over hadd (fixed punishment), nikah (marriage), and riq (slavery) is absolutely impermissible because these involve sacred rights of Allah or inalienable personal status.
These are not just disliked; the sulh is batil (void).
3
Examine the defective consideration scenario
The text gives examples: if the sulh consideration (e.g., currency) is found to be debased (ستوقة) or counterfeit (نبهرجة), the ruling depends on whether the parties have parted. If they already parted, the sulh is voided; if not, the sulh stands and the claimant returns an equivalent.
Also applies to destruction of the consideration before delivery—treated like reclamation.
4
Apply the rule for unknown claims
If the claim is in an unknown (majhul) house and part is reclaimed, no refund is due. But if the claim is specific (a known house) and the sulh is for a piece of it, it is invalid unless an additional dirham is added or a release from the rest is explicitly mentioned.
This prevents partial settlement without full discharge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
الصلح جائز عن دعوى المال والمنفعة(۱) والجناية بخلاف الحد ومن النكاح والرق
قبله، كما لو وجدها ستوقة أو نبهرجة بخلاف ما إذا كان من غير الجنس كالدنانير هنا إذا استحقت بعد الافتراق فإن الصلح يبطل، وإن كان قبله رجع بمثلها ولا يبطل الصلح كالفلوس (وهلاك بدل الصلح قبل التسليم كاستحقاقه في فصل الإقرار وفصل الإنكار والسكوت) وإن ادعى حقاً في دار مجهولاً فصولح على شيء ثم استحق بعض الدار لم يرد شيئاً من العوض، وإن ادعى داراً فصالحه على قطعة منها لم يصح حتى يزيد درهماً في بدل الصلح أو يلحق به ذكر البراءة عن دعوى الباقي والله أعلم.

فصل
(الصلح جائز عن دعوى المال مطلقاً (والمنفعة) كصلح المستأجر مع المؤجر عند إنكاره الإجارة أو مقدار المدة المدعى بها أو الأجرة وكذا الورثة إذا صالحوا الموصى له بالخدمة على مال مطلقاً أو المنافع إن اختلف جنسها فإنه يجوز لا إن اتحد. وإن صالحوه على ثوب فوجد به عيباً كان له رده والرجوع بالموصى به، وليس له بيع المصالح عليه قبل قبضه وله الاستبدال به قبل قبضه إن كان مما لا يتعين بالتعيين. ولو اشترى الوارث منه الخدمة لم يجز، ولو قال أعطيتك هذه الدراهم مكان خدمتك أو عوضاً عنها أو بدلاً أو على أن تتركها جاز صلحاً كقوله أهب لك هذه الدراهم على أن تهب لي خدمتك بشرط قبض الدراهم. ولو كان الوارث اثنين فصالحه أحدهما على عشرة دراهم على إن جعل له خدمة هذا الخادم خاصة دون شريكه لم يجز، ولو باع الورثة العبد فأجاز صاحب الخدمة البيع بطلت خدمته ولم يكن له في
Section: Sulh is permissible regarding a claim of property, benefit, and crime, unlike hadd, marriage, and slavery before it. For example, if he finds it [the currency] to be debased or counterfeit. Contrary to if it is from a different genus, like dinars here, if they are reclaimed after parting, then the sulh is voided; if before, he returns the like and the sulh is not voided, like fulus. The destruction of the sulh consideration before delivery is like its reclamation in the section of acknowledgment, denial, and silence. If he claims a right in an unknown house and makes sulh for something, then part of the house is reclaimed, he does not return anything from the consideration. If he claims a house and makes sulh for a piece of it, it is not valid unless he adds a dirham to the consideration or includes a mention of release from the rest of the claim. And Allah knows best. Section: Sulh is permissible regarding a claim of property absolutely (and benefit), like the sulh of a tenant with the landlord when he denies the lease or the claimed duration or rent. Likewise, the heirs if they make sulh with the legatee of service for property absolutely, or benefits if their types differ, then it is permissible; not if they are the same. If they make sulh with him for a garment and he finds a defect, he has the right to return it and revert to the bequeathed. He may not sell the subject of sulh before taking possession, but he may exchange it before taking possession if it is non-specific. If the heir buys the service from him, it is not permissible. If he says, 'I give you these dirhams in place of your service, or as compensation for it, or as a substitute, or on condition that you leave it,' it is valid as sulh, like his saying, 'I give you these dirhams as a gift on condition that you gift me your service,' with the condition of taking possession of the dirhams. If there are two heirs and one of them makes sulh with him for ten dirhams on the condition that the service of this particular servant be for him alone, excluding his partner, it is not valid. If the heirs sell the slave and the owner of the service ratifies the sale, his service is voided and he has no
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage contains two consecutive sections (fasl) from the Book of Sulh. The first section is a memorization anchor ruling that sulh is permissible over claims of property, benefits (manafi'), and crimes (jinaya), but it is not permissible over claims of hadd (fixed punishments), marriage (nikah), or slavery (riq). The reason is that these latter rights are sacred or involve inviolable aspects that cannot be compromised via sulh. The section then provides examples: if the currency given in sulh is found to be debased or counterfeit, the ruling depends on whether the parties have parted. If they parted after taking possession, the sulh is voided because the consideration was invalid; if not yet parted, the sulh stands and the claimant returns the like. Similarly, if the consideration is destroyed before delivery, it is treated like reclamation. A practical rule is given: if someone claims a right in a house that is unknown (majhul) and makes sulh, then part of the house is reclaimed, he does not return any part of the consideration, because the claim was unknown. But if the claim is specific (a known house) and he settles for a piece, it is invalid unless he adds a dirham to the consideration or explicitly includes release from the rest. This is because the settlement would otherwise cover part of the claimed property without full discharge. The second section elaborates on sulh over benefits, providing that it is absolutely permissible over property, and over benefits provided the types differ. Examples include sulh between a tenant and landlord when the lease is denied, or between heirs and a legatee of service (e.g., the right to use a slave). If the legatee is paid off with property, it is valid. If the sulh is for a garment and a defect is found, the legatee can return it and revert to the original bequest. The subject of sulh cannot be sold before possession but can be exchanged if non-specific. The section also discusses wording: saying 'I give you these dirhams in place of your service' is valid as sulh, akin to a conditional gift. However, if there are two heirs and only one makes sulh for the service of a specific slave exclusively, it is not valid because it disrupts the co-ownership. Finally, if the heirs sell the slave and the legatee of service ratifies the sale, the service right is extinguished, and the legatee has no further claim (the rest of the ruling is cut off).

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A contract to settle a dispute by mutual compromise, often involving a payment to drop a claim.
منفعة (manfa'ah): A benefit or usufruct, such as service or rental use.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for certain crimes (e.g., zina, theft).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, sulh is NOT permissible for which of the following?
A) Claim for a debt (mal)
B) Claim for unpaid rent (manfa'ah)
C) Claim for a fixed punishment (hadd)
D) Claim for injury resulting in compensation

Key Takeaway
Sulh is a powerful dispute resolution tool but cannot be used to compromise hadd, marriage, or slavery rights.

Sulh over Benefits: Conditions and Examples
Details sulh over benefits with conditions and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions for a valid sulh over benefits (manafi'), including the rules for differing types of benefits, defective subject matter, and permissible wording.

Core Idea
Sulh over benefits requires that the benefit types differ or the consideration be property; identical benefits void the sulh.

Benefits, such as service or rental use, can be the subject of sulh, but with important specifications. The second fasl of the passage provides detailed scenarios: from tenant-landlord disputes to legatee of service. Understanding these conditions prevents invalid compromises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of benefit sulh
The text begins 'الصلح جائز عن دعوى المال مطلقاً (والمنفعة)'. Benefit sulh is allowed overall, but then distinguishes: if the benefit types differ, sulh is valid; if they are the same type, it is invalid. Locate the condition: 'إن اختلف جنسها فإنه يجوز لا إن اتحد'.
Differing types means different kinds of services, not just different durations.
2
Analyze the tenant-landlord example
The text gives a scenario: a tenant and landlord dispute over the existence or terms of a lease. They can make sulh, presumably for a sum to end the dispute. This is valid because the benefit (use of property) is being settled.
The exact details of the lease can be denied; the sulh creates a new agreement.
3
Examine the legatee of service scenario
Heirs can make sulh with a legatee who was bequeathed the service of a slave. If the sulh is for a specific property (e.g., a garment), and a defect is found, the legatee can return it and revert to the bequest. The sulh consideration cannot be sold before possession but can be exchanged if non-specific.
This shows that the sulh is treated like a sale for some purposes.
4
Learn the permissible wording
The text provides valid phrases: 'I give you these dirhams in place of your service' or 'I give you these dirhams as a gift on condition that you gift me your service'. These are valid as sulh, but only with immediate possession of the dirhams.
The wording must clearly indicate an exchange, not a sale.
5
Handle multiple heirs
If there are two heirs and only one makes sulh with the legatee for the service of a specific slave exclusively, it is invalid because it disrupts co-ownership. The legatee's service right is against the estate, not an individual heir.
This protects the rights of all heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
الصلح جائز عن دعوى المال والمنفعة(۱) والجناية بخلاف الحد ومن النكاح والرق
قبله، كما لو وجدها ستوقة أو نبهرجة بخلاف ما إذا كان من غير الجنس كالدنانير هنا إذا استحقت بعد الافتراق فإن الصلح يبطل، وإن كان قبله رجع بمثلها ولا يبطل الصلح كالفلوس (وهلاك بدل الصلح قبل التسليم كاستحقاقه في فصل الإقرار وفصل الإنكار والسكوت) وإن ادعى حقاً في دار مجهولاً فصولح على شيء ثم استحق بعض الدار لم يرد شيئاً من العوض، وإن ادعى داراً فصالحه على قطعة منها لم يصح حتى يزيد درهماً في بدل الصلح أو يلحق به ذكر البراءة عن دعوى الباقي والله أعلم.

فصل
(الصلح جائز عن دعوى المال مطلقاً (والمنفعة) كصلح المستأجر مع المؤجر عند إنكاره الإجارة أو مقدار المدة المدعى بها أو الأجرة وكذا الورثة إذا صالحوا الموصى له بالخدمة على مال مطلقاً أو المنافع إن اختلف جنسها فإنه يجوز لا إن اتحد. وإن صالحوه على ثوب فوجد به عيباً كان له رده والرجوع بالموصى به، وليس له بيع المصالح عليه قبل قبضه وله الاستبدال به قبل قبضه إن كان مما لا يتعين بالتعيين. ولو اشترى الوارث منه الخدمة لم يجز، ولو قال أعطيتك هذه الدراهم مكان خدمتك أو عوضاً عنها أو بدلاً أو على أن تتركها جاز صلحاً كقوله أهب لك هذه الدراهم على أن تهب لي خدمتك بشرط قبض الدراهم. ولو كان الوارث اثنين فصالحه أحدهما على عشرة دراهم على إن جعل له خدمة هذا الخادم خاصة دون شريكه لم يجز، ولو باع الورثة العبد فأجاز صاحب الخدمة البيع بطلت خدمته ولم يكن له في
Section: Sulh is permissible regarding a claim of property, benefit, and crime, unlike hadd, marriage, and slavery before it. For example, if he finds it [the currency] to be debased or counterfeit. Contrary to if it is from a different genus, like dinars here, if they are reclaimed after parting, then the sulh is voided; if before, he returns the like and the sulh is not voided, like fulus. The destruction of the sulh consideration before delivery is like its reclamation in the section of acknowledgment, denial, and silence. If he claims a right in an unknown house and makes sulh for something, then part of the house is reclaimed, he does not return anything from the consideration. If he claims a house and makes sulh for a piece of it, it is not valid unless he adds a dirham to the consideration or includes a mention of release from the rest of the claim. And Allah knows best. Section: Sulh is permissible regarding a claim of property absolutely (and benefit), like the sulh of a tenant with the landlord when he denies the lease or the claimed duration or rent. Likewise, the heirs if they make sulh with the legatee of service for property absolutely, or benefits if their types differ, then it is permissible; not if they are the same. If they make sulh with him for a garment and he finds a defect, he has the right to return it and revert to the bequeathed. He may not sell the subject of sulh before taking possession, but he may exchange it before taking possession if it is non-specific. If the heir buys the service from him, it is not permissible. If he says, 'I give you these dirhams in place of your service, or as compensation for it, or as a substitute, or on condition that you leave it,' it is valid as sulh, like his saying, 'I give you these dirhams as a gift on condition that you gift me your service,' with the condition of taking possession of the dirhams. If there are two heirs and one of them makes sulh with him for ten dirhams on the condition that the service of this particular servant be for him alone, excluding his partner, it is not valid. If the heirs sell the slave and the owner of the service ratifies the sale, his service is voided and he has no
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage contains two consecutive sections (fasl) from the Book of Sulh. The first section is a memorization anchor ruling that sulh is permissible over claims of property, benefits (manafi'), and crimes (jinaya), but it is not permissible over claims of hadd (fixed punishments), marriage (nikah), or slavery (riq). The reason is that these latter rights are sacred or involve inviolable aspects that cannot be compromised via sulh. The section then provides examples: if the currency given in sulh is found to be debased or counterfeit, the ruling depends on whether the parties have parted. If they parted after taking possession, the sulh is voided because the consideration was invalid; if not yet parted, the sulh stands and the claimant returns the like. Similarly, if the consideration is destroyed before delivery, it is treated like reclamation. A practical rule is given: if someone claims a right in a house that is unknown (majhul) and makes sulh, then part of the house is reclaimed, he does not return any part of the consideration, because the claim was unknown. But if the claim is specific (a known house) and he settles for a piece, it is invalid unless he adds a dirham to the consideration or explicitly includes release from the rest. This is because the settlement would otherwise cover part of the claimed property without full discharge. The second section elaborates on sulh over benefits, providing that it is absolutely permissible over property, and over benefits provided the types differ. Examples include sulh between a tenant and landlord when the lease is denied, or between heirs and a legatee of service (e.g., the right to use a slave). If the legatee is paid off with property, it is valid. If the sulh is for a garment and a defect is found, the legatee can return it and revert to the original bequest. The subject of sulh cannot be sold before possession but can be exchanged if non-specific. The section also discusses wording: saying 'I give you these dirhams in place of your service' is valid as sulh, akin to a conditional gift. However, if there are two heirs and only one makes sulh for the service of a specific slave exclusively, it is not valid because it disrupts the co-ownership. Finally, if the heirs sell the slave and the legatee of service ratifies the sale, the service right is extinguished, and the legatee has no further claim (the rest of the ruling is cut off).

Key Terms
منفعة (manfa'ah): A benefit or usufruct, such as service or rental use.
موصى له بالخدمة (musa lahu bil-khidma): A person who is bequeathed the service of a slave (or animal) in a will.
بدل الصلح (badal al-sulh): The consideration given in a sulh contract to drop a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute over the service of a slave, the heirs offer the legatee a specific garment as compensation. The legatee later finds the garment has a defect. According to the passage, what can the legatee do?
A) Accept the garment and forfeit the service.
B) Return the garment and revert to the original bequest of service.
C) Sue the heirs for a different garment.
D) Demand the cash value of the garment.

Key Takeaway
Sulh over benefits requires that the benefit types differ or the consideration be property; identical benefits invalidate the sulh.

Sulh on Property Claims: Scope and Effect of Loss of Consideration
Opening rulings of Kitab al-Sulh: definition and conditions of sulh regarding property and usufruct, and effect of loss/claim of consideration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the scope of valid sulh in Hanafi fiqh and determine the effect of loss or third-party claim of the consideration before delivery.

Core Idea
Loss of the sulh consideration before delivery reverts the case to the original claim, just as if a third party claimed ownership.

This lesson introduces the fundamentals of sulh (amicable settlement) in Hanafi law. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies which claims are eligible for sulh and, crucially, what happens if the consideration is destroyed or claimed by another before delivery. Understanding these rules is essential for anyone involved in dispute resolution within the Islamic legal framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of valid sulh
Determine which types of claims can be settled via sulh (property, usufruct, criminal acts) and which are excluded (hudud, marriage, slavery before the fact).
The exclusion of hudud is based on the principle that claims of Allah cannot be compromised.
2
Understand the effect of loss or istihqaq of consideration
Read the ruling that destruction of the consideration before delivery is treated like istihqaq (third-party claim). Both cause the sulh to be invalidated and the case reverts to the original claim.
This applies in chapters of iqrar, inkar, and sukot.
3
Analyze the special case of different type of consideration
If the consideration is of a different type (e.g., dinars instead of dirhams) and it is claimed after separation, the sulh is invalid. If before separation, the claimant returns a similar item and the sulh remains valid.
Compare with the case of fulus (copper coins) where the ruling is the same as before separation.
4
Apply the rulings to two concrete cases
Case 1: Claiming an unspecified right in a house and making sulh; then part of the house is claimed by a third party. Ruling: no compensation is returned. Case 2: Claiming a whole house and settling on a piece; the sulh is invalid unless a dirham is added or acquittal from the remaining claim is mentioned.
These cases illustrate the importance of specificity in the claim and consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه أو بعضه رجع إلى الدعوى في كله أو بعضه وهلاك بدل الصلح قبل التسليم كاستحقاقه في الفصلين . فصل (الصلح جائز عن دعوى المال والمنفعة(۱) والجناية بخلاف الحد ومن النكاح والرق قبله، كما لو وجدها ستوقة أو نبهرجة بخلاف ما إذا كان من غير الجنس كالدنانير هنا إذا استحقت بعد الافتراق فإن الصلح يبطل، وإن كان قبله رجع بمثلها ولا يبطل الصلح كالفلوس (وهلاك بدل الصلح قبل التسليم كاستحقاقه في فصل الإقرار وفصل الإنكار والسكوت) وإن ادعى حقاً في دار مجهولاً فصولح على شيء ثم استحق بعض الدار لم يرد شيئاً من العوض، وإن ادعى داراً فصالحه على قطعة منها لم يصح حتى يزيد درهماً في بدل الصلح أو يلحق به ذكر البراءة عن دعوى الباقي والله أعلم. (۱) قد أثبتا المتن في هذه الملزمة طبق ما في المتون وإن تخالف مع المتن الذي كتب عليه الشارح فليعلم.
Upon him or some of it, he returns to the claim in all or some of it, and the destruction of the consideration of sulh before delivery is like its being claimed (istihqaq) in the two chapters. Chapter: Sulh is permitted for a claim of property and usufruct and criminal acts, except for hadd, and from marriage and slavery before it, as if he found it defective or counterfeit, contrary to if it is from another type like dinar here if it is claimed after separation, then the sulh is invalid, and if it was before, he returns to its like and the sulh does not become invalid like fulus. And the destruction of the consideration of sulh before delivery is like its being claimed in the chapter of iqrar and chapter of inkar and silence. If he claimed a right in a house unknown, and he made sulh on something, then part of the house was claimed, he does not return anything from the compensation. If he claimed a house and made sulh with him on a piece of it, it is not valid until he adds a dirham in the consideration of sulh or attaches to it a mention of acquittal from the remaining claim. And Allah knows best. (1) We have recorded the matn in this booklet as per what is in the texts, even if it contradicts the matn on which the commentator wrote, so let it be known.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on sulh (amicable settlement). The first line addresses a scenario where the sulh is partially invalidated: if the consideration (badal al-sulh) is destroyed before delivery, the case reverts to the original claim. This is analogous to istihqaq (the consideration being claimed by a third party). The chapter heading states that sulh is valid for claims of property, usufruct, and criminal acts (jinaayah), but not for hadd punishments, nor for issues of marriage or slavery before the fact (i.e., before the marriage or slavery is established). Examples: if the consideration is found defective (satouqah?) or counterfeit (nabahrajah), the ruling follows accordingly; but if the consideration is of a different type (e.g., dinars instead of dirhams) and is claimed after separation, the sulh is invalid. If claimed before separation, the claimant returns a similar item and the sulh remains valid, as with fulus (copper coins). The principle that loss of consideration before delivery equals its being claimed by a third party applies in the chapters of iqrar (acknowledgment), inkar (denial), and sukot (silence). Two specific cases: (1) If someone claims a right in a house but the house is unspecified (majhool) and sulh is made, then part of the house is claimed by a third party, no compensation is returned. (2) If someone claims a whole house and settles on a piece of it, the settlement is invalid unless he adds a dirham to the consideration or includes a clause of acquittal (bara'ah) from the remaining claim. The footnote clarifies that the matn recorded here may differ from the matn used by the commentator; this is a textual note.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): An amicable settlement or compromise between two parties in a dispute, involving a consideration (badal) to end the claim.
بدل الصلح (badal al-sulh): The consideration given in a sulh agreement; its loss before delivery nullifies the sulh or reverts to the original claim.
استحقاق (istihqaq): A third party's claim of ownership over the consideration, which nullifies the sulh similarly to loss before delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the consideration in a sulh agreement is destroyed before delivery, what is the effect according to this passage?
A) The sulh becomes void and the claim reverts to its original state.
B) The sulh remains valid and a substitute consideration must be given.
C) The parties must make a new sulh with a different consideration.
D) The destruction is ignored and the sulh continues.

Key Takeaway
Sulh is valid only for claims of property, usufruct, and criminal acts; loss of the consideration before delivery reverts the case to the original claim.

Compromise on Debt: Isqat vs Mu'awada
Rulings and principle on debt compromise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between isqat (forfeiture) and mu'awada (exchange) in debt compromise and state the conditions under which each type is valid.

Core Idea
Compromise on debt is valid if the settlement is less (isqat) or of a different type (mu'awada), but invalid if it involves riba or uncertainty.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational principle of compromising debts in the Hanafi school. The key distinction is whether the settlement is a forfeiture of part of the debt or an exchange for something else. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq provides clear examples to parse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Compromise on debt is permissible (ja'iz) unless specific invalidities are present.
2
Categorize the settlement
If the compromise amount is less than the owed (in value, quality, or one of two items), it is isqat (forfeiture of the difference). If it is more or of a different type, it is mu'awada (exchange).
3
Apply to examples
Half of a thousand (isqat valid); deferred for immediate (mu'awada valid); black dirhams for white immediate (invalid due to riba risk).
4
Extract the principle
The text states: 'Wa al-aslu annahu...' which is the key to understanding all subsequent rulings.
Memorize the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلح باب الصلح في الدين. ألف على نصفه أو على ألف مؤجل جاز وعلى دنانير مؤجلة أو عن ألف صالح عن مؤجل أو سود على نصف حال أو بيض لا ومن له على آخر ألف فقال أد غداً نصفه باء من الفضل ففعل برئ وإلا لا ومن قال لا أقر لك بمالك حتى تؤخره على أنك بريء عني أو تحط ففعل صح عليه . ألف فصل في الدين المشترك دين بينهما صالح أحدهما عن نصيبه على ثوب لشريكه أن يتبع المديون بنصفه أو عن درهم سود على ألف بيض مقبوضة أو ألف درهم ومائة دينار على مائة حالة أو ألف مؤجلة بدل الكتابة على خمسمائة حالة (جاز) وعن ألف مؤجلة على مؤجلة أو عن سود على عن ألف خمسمائة حالة في غير المكاتب أو عن ألف درهم على دنانير مؤجلة أو خمسمائة بيض أو عن ألف على طعام موصوف في الذمة مؤجل أو غير مؤجل غير مقبوض لم يجز. والأصل أنه متى كان الذي وقع عليه الصلح أدون من حقه قدراً أو وصفاً أو في أنه إحداهما فهو إسقاط للبعض واستيفاء للباقي، وإن كان أزيد منه بمعنى دخل فيه ما لا يستحق من وصف أو ما هو بمعنى الوصف كتعجيل المؤجل وعن اختلاف الجنس فهو معاوضة. ويجوز الصلح بدراهم عن دراهم مجهولة في الذمة ومن له على آخر ألف فقال أد غداً نصفه على أنك بريء من الفضل ففعل برئ وإلا لا وكذا لو قال وأنت بريء من الزيادة على أنك إن لم تدفعها إلي غداً فلا تبرأ عن الباقي، ولو قال أبرأتك كذا على أن عن تعطيني كذا فإنه يبرأ وإن لم يؤد غداً، وكذا لو قال أد إلي كذا على أنك بريء من باقيه ولم يوقت، ولو قال إن أديت إلي خمسمائة أو إذا أديت أو متى أديت فأنت بريء من الباقي لم مطلقاً صحة تعليق البراءة بصريح الشرط بخلاف ما إذا كان بمعناه (ومن قال لعدم لآخر لا أقر لك بمالك حتى تؤخره عني أو تحط بعضه ففعل صح) إن قال ذلك سراً وإن قال علانية يؤخذ به ولو ادعى ألفاً فجحده فقال اقرر لي بها على أن أحط منها مائة أو على أن حططت منها مائة فأقر جاز بخلاف قوله على أن أعطيك مائة لأن الإقرار لا يستحق به البدل، ولو قال إن أقررت لي حططت منها مائة فأقر صح الإقرار لا الحط؛ كذا في المجتبى والله أعلم.
Book of Compromise, Chapter on Compromise regarding Debt. One thousand on its half or on one thousand deferred is permissible. And on deferred dinars or on one thousand, he compromised from deferred or black (dirhams) on half immediate or white (dirhams) is not permissible. And he who has a thousand owed by another and said: 'Pay tomorrow half of it with (something) extra', and he did, he is discharged; otherwise no. And he who said: 'I will not acknowledge your right until you defer (it) from me or deduct (some)' and he did, it is valid. ... The principle: Whenever what the compromise is made upon is less than his right in amount, description, or in that it is one of them, it is a forfeiture of some and collection of the remainder. If it is more than it, in the sense that it includes what he does not deserve in description or what is equivalent to description like expediting the deferred, or if it is of a different type, then it is an exchange. ... And he who said: 'I discharged you from such-and-such on condition that you give me such-and-such', then he is discharged even if he does not pay tomorrow. ... (And he who said to another: 'I will not acknowledge your right until you defer it from me or deduct some', and he did, it is valid) if he said it secretly; if he said it publicly, it is taken from him. ...
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings on compromise (sulh) regarding debt, characteristic of a matn requiring careful parsing. It begins by stating that compromising a debt of one thousand for half of it or for a deferred thousand is valid (jā'iz). However, if the compromise is for deferred dinars or for black dirhams against immediate payment or white dirhams, it is not valid. The key principle is that if the settlement is for less than the owed amount (in value, quality, or one of two items), it constitutes a partial forfeiture (isqāt) and collection of the remainder. If it is for more (e.g., includes a better quality or earlier payment), or if the type differs, it is considered an exchange (mu'āwaḍah). The text then presents specific scenarios: a conditional offer to pay half tomorrow with extra, where fulfillment discharges the debt; an acknowledgment withheld pending deferment or reduction, which if done secretly is valid but if publicly is binding; and cases where the acknowledgment is conditional on a reduction, which is valid except when the condition is to give a payment (since acknowledgment is not a commutative contract). The passage concludes with a ruling that if someone says 'If you acknowledge, I will deduct a hundred', the acknowledgment is valid but the deduction is not. All this is from al-Mujtabā, and Allah knows best.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A settlement or compromise between parties to end a dispute, often involving reduction or change of debt.
إسقاط (isqāṭ): Forfeiture or dropping of a right, such as part of the debt.
معاوضة (mu'āwaḍah): A commutative exchange where one thing is given for another.
براءة (barā'ah): Discharge or immunity from liability, e.g., when a debtor pays as agreed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is valid as isqat?
A) Compromising a thousand for half immediate
B) Compromising a thousand for deferred dinars
C) Compromising black dirhams for white immediate
D) Compromising a thousand for a thousand deferred

Key Takeaway
Compromise on debt is permissible, but its validity depends on whether it is a forfeiture (isqat) or exchange (mu'awada), each with distinct conditions.

Conditional Compromise and Discharge
Rulings on conditional compromise and discharge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on conditional offers to pay part of a debt with extra, and on conditional acknowledgments tied to deferment or reduction.

Core Idea
A conditional offer to pay half tomorrow with extra discharges the debt if fulfilled; an acknowledgment withheld pending deferment or reduction is valid only if said secretly.

This lesson examines two types of conditional scenarios in debt compromise: offers to pay part of the debt with something extra, and acknowledgments that are conditioned on deferment or reduction. The matn provides precise rulings on when the debtor is discharged and when the creditor's statement is binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of the conditional offer
The creditor says 'Pay half tomorrow with extra' — if the debtor pays, he is discharged; otherwise the original debt remains.
2
Analyze the fulfillment condition
Payment of half with extra is considered full settlement if executed. If not, the debt is not reduced.
3
Distinguish the acknowledgment condition
The creditor says 'I will not acknowledge until you defer or deduct' — if said secretly, the acknowledgment is valid but not binding; if said publicly, it is binding.
4
Understand the principle of discharge as an immediate act
A statement like 'I discharge you on condition that you give me such-and-such' results in immediate discharge, regardless of later payment.
5
Apply to the final scenario
If acknowledgment is conditioned on reduction, the acknowledgment is valid but the reduction is not, because reduction depends on acknowledgment which is already complete.

كتاب الصلح باب الصلح في الدين. ألف على نصفه أو على ألف مؤجل جاز وعلى دنانير مؤجلة أو عن ألف صالح عن مؤجل أو سود على نصف حال أو بيض لا ومن له على آخر ألف فقال أد غداً نصفه باء من الفضل ففعل برئ وإلا لا ومن قال لا أقر لك بمالك حتى تؤخره على أنك بريء عني أو تحط ففعل صح عليه . ألف فصل في الدين المشترك دين بينهما صالح أحدهما عن نصيبه على ثوب لشريكه أن يتبع المديون بنصفه أو عن درهم سود على ألف بيض مقبوضة أو ألف درهم ومائة دينار على مائة حالة أو ألف مؤجلة بدل الكتابة على خمسمائة حالة (جاز) وعن ألف مؤجلة على مؤجلة أو عن سود على عن ألف خمسمائة حالة في غير المكاتب أو عن ألف درهم على دنانير مؤجلة أو خمسمائة بيض أو عن ألف على طعام موصوف في الذمة مؤجل أو غير مؤجل غير مقبوض لم يجز. والأصل أنه متى كان الذي وقع عليه الصلح أدون من حقه قدراً أو وصفاً أو في أنه إحداهما فهو إسقاط للبعض واستيفاء للباقي، وإن كان أزيد منه بمعنى دخل فيه ما لا يستحق من وصف أو ما هو بمعنى الوصف كتعجيل المؤجل وعن اختلاف الجنس فهو معاوضة. ويجوز الصلح بدراهم عن دراهم مجهولة في الذمة ومن له على آخر ألف فقال أد غداً نصفه على أنك بريء من الفضل ففعل برئ وإلا لا وكذا لو قال وأنت بريء من الزيادة على أنك إن لم تدفعها إلي غداً فلا تبرأ عن الباقي، ولو قال أبرأتك كذا على أن عن تعطيني كذا فإنه يبرأ وإن لم يؤد غداً، وكذا لو قال أد إلي كذا على أنك بريء من باقيه ولم يوقت، ولو قال إن أديت إلي خمسمائة أو إذا أديت أو متى أديت فأنت بريء من الباقي لم مطلقاً صحة تعليق البراءة بصريح الشرط بخلاف ما إذا كان بمعناه (ومن قال لعدم لآخر لا أقر لك بمالك حتى تؤخره عني أو تحط بعضه ففعل صح) إن قال ذلك سراً وإن قال علانية يؤخذ به ولو ادعى ألفاً فجحده فقال اقرر لي بها على أن أحط منها مائة أو على أن حططت منها مائة فأقر جاز بخلاف قوله على أن أعطيك مائة لأن الإقرار لا يستحق به البدل، ولو قال إن أقررت لي حططت منها مائة فأقر صح الإقرار لا الحط؛ كذا في المجتبى والله أعلم.
Book of Compromise, Chapter on Compromise regarding Debt. One thousand on its half or on one thousand deferred is permissible. And on deferred dinars or on one thousand, he compromised from deferred or black (dirhams) on half immediate or white (dirhams) is not permissible. And he who has a thousand owed by another and said: 'Pay tomorrow half of it with (something) extra', and he did, he is discharged; otherwise no. And he who said: 'I will not acknowledge your right until you defer (it) from me or deduct (some)' and he did, it is valid. ... The principle: Whenever what the compromise is made upon is less than his right in amount, description, or in that it is one of them, it is a forfeiture of some and collection of the remainder. If it is more than it, in the sense that it includes what he does not deserve in description or what is equivalent to description like expediting the deferred, or if it is of a different type, then it is an exchange. ... And he who said: 'I discharged you from such-and-such on condition that you give me such-and-such', then he is discharged even if he does not pay tomorrow. ... (And he who said to another: 'I will not acknowledge your right until you defer it from me or deduct some', and he did, it is valid) if he said it secretly; if he said it publicly, it is taken from him. ...
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings on compromise (sulh) regarding debt, characteristic of a matn requiring careful parsing. It begins by stating that compromising a debt of one thousand for half of it or for a deferred thousand is valid (jā'iz). However, if the compromise is for deferred dinars or for black dirhams against immediate payment or white dirhams, it is not valid. The key principle is that if the settlement is for less than the owed amount (in value, quality, or one of two items), it constitutes a partial forfeiture (isqāt) and collection of the remainder. If it is for more (e.g., includes a better quality or earlier payment), or if the type differs, it is considered an exchange (mu'āwaḍah). The text then presents specific scenarios: a conditional offer to pay half tomorrow with extra, where fulfillment discharges the debt; an acknowledgment withheld pending deferment or reduction, which if done secretly is valid but if publicly is binding; and cases where the acknowledgment is conditional on a reduction, which is valid except when the condition is to give a payment (since acknowledgment is not a commutative contract). The passage concludes with a ruling that if someone says 'If you acknowledge, I will deduct a hundred', the acknowledgment is valid but the deduction is not. All this is from al-Mujtabā, and Allah knows best.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A settlement or compromise between parties to end a dispute, often involving reduction or change of debt.
إسقاط (isqāṭ): Forfeiture or dropping of a right, such as part of the debt.
معاوضة (mu'āwaḍah): A commutative exchange where one thing is given for another.
براءة (barā'ah): Discharge or immunity from liability, e.g., when a debtor pays as agreed.
إبراء (ibrā'): A unilateral discharge of debt, often used synonymously with barā'ah in the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a creditor says 'I discharge you from the debt on condition that you give me a gold coin', what is the ruling?
A) Discharge is conditional and not effective until coin given.
B) Discharge is effective immediately.
C) Discharge is invalid because condition is not met.
D) The coin must be given first.

Key Takeaway
Conditional discharge statements may take effect immediately or only upon fulfillment, depending on phrasing; public statements about acknowledgment are binding.

The Partner's Option (Khiyar al-Sharik) in Shared Debt Compromise
Explains the khiyar al-sharik when one partner compromises a shared debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the khiyar al-sharik (option of the partner) when one partner compromises a shared debt, and apply the two options to determine the legal consequences for both partners.

Core Idea
When one partner compromises a shared debt, the other partner holds an option to pursue the debtor or the compromising partner.

In Hanafi fiqh, a debt jointly owned by partners (dayn mushtarak) is treated with special care to protect each partner's share. When one partner settles the debt with the debtor through a compromise (sulh), the other partner's interests are safeguarded by granting him an option known as khiyar al-sharik. This lesson, drawn from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq's commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, unpacks the rules governing this option, the subsequent choices of the compromising partner, and a legal stratagem (hila) to avoid unfair recourse. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly advising on joint financial claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shared debt and the compromise act
Recognize that a dayn mushtarak arises from a single cause (e.g., price of a jointly sold item) and belongs to two or more partners. One partner then makes a compromise (sulh) with the debtor, settling for a different type or the same type of asset, or for a reduced amount.
The compromise may be on acknowledgment, silence, or denial of the debt.
2
Determine the non-settling partner's option (khiyar al-sharik)
The non-settling partner has two choices: (1) follow the debtor and demand his share directly, or (2) follow the settling partner and claim from him. This option exists whether the compromise is on a different type (ghayr jins) or the same type (jins) of the debt.
The settling partner has no corresponding option; his act is considered like receiving part of the debt.
3
Analyze the settling partner's subsequent options if pursued
If the non-settling partner chooses to follow him, the settling partner may either: (a) pay the non-settling partner his share of the settlement amount (hissatuhu min al-musalah alayh), or (b) guarantee him a quarter of the original debt (rub' al-dayn).
The quarter represents the non-settling partner's share of the guarantee arising from the compromise.
4
Apply the legal stratagem (hila) to avoid recourse
To prevent the non-settling partner from pursuing him, the settling partner can use a hila: the debtor gifts the settling partner the amount of his share, and the settling partner then discharges the debtor, or the settling partner sells a small item to the debtor for the amount of his share and then discharges him after receiving the price.
This stratagem effectively transfers the settling partner's right without creating a direct claim against him.
5
Consider special cases: loss, deferment, reduction
If the non-settling partner chooses to follow the debtor and the debtor becomes insolvent or dies, the partner has recourse against the settling partner for half of what he received (not the specific coins). Deferment (ta'jil) by one partner is valid only if he is the original lender (in 'inan partnership) or any partner (in mufawadah). Reduction (hatt) by one partner binds only his share unless he is the contracting party.
These nuances ensure that the rights of both partners are balanced according to the nature of their partnership.

Chapter on Shared Debt: A single transaction, one 'ayn or multiple items, but the shared debt due to a single cause like price of a sold item... The saying: 'And if he compromises on its type, the partner has an option' etc. And the one making the compromise has no option because it is like receiving part of the debt. He returns and takes half the garment from his partner unless the partner pays him a quarter of the debt. If he receives his share, the partner shares with him in it, and both go after the debtor for the remainder. If he buys something with his share, he is liable for a quarter of the debt. ... And if the partners (heirs) bring out one of them from a commodity or real estate with money, or from gold with silver or vice versa, it is valid, little or much. ... If he compromises with him on its type, the partner has the option: if he wishes, he may pursue the debtor, or participate, then both return upon the debtor for the remainder as if he had received. If he chooses to pursue the debtor and then his share is lost (debtor dies insolvent), he has recourse against the receiver for half of what he received, even if from someone else. ... And if one of them grants a deferment, if the debt was not obligatory by a contract of each (e.g., inherited deferred debt), the deferment is void. If it was obligatory by one's lending, and they are partners in an 'inān company, then if the one who made the loan grants deferment, it is valid for the entire debt; if the other grants it, it is not valid even for his share. If they are partners in a mufāwaḍah company, whichever grants deferment, it is valid like an agent selling on credit grants deferment of the price. ... And if one of the parties to a salam contract compromises regarding the subject matter... In a marginal note: 'Min ghayrihi' means other than what he received. The statement of al-Zayla'ī: He has recourse against him as in ḥawālah, but he cannot have recourse on the very dirhams received because his right in them has fallen by delivery, so his right does not return by loss; it returns to his liability in kind.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the chapter of shared debt, explaining the consequences when one partner (sharīk) compromises the common debt with the debtor. The passage begins by referencing a statement from the matn: 'If he compromises on its type, the partner has an option.' The sharīk who did not compromise (the non-settling partner) has two options: either he can follow the debtor for his share, or he can follow his partner (the one who settled). If he chooses to follow his partner, the settling partner then has two options: either pay him his share of what was settled for, or pay him a quarter of the debt (i.e., his share of the original debt? Actually, the text says 'ina shā'a dafa'a lahu ḥiṣṣatahu min al-muṣālaḥi 'alayhi wa in shā'a ḍamina lahu rub'a al-dayn' meaning the settling partner can either give the non-settling partner his share of the settlement amount, or guarantee him a quarter of the debt). The ruling applies whether the compromise was based on acknowledgment, silence, or denial. The passage then provides a legal stratagem (ḥīla) for the non-settling partner to avoid recourse against him: the debtor can gift the settling partner the amount of his share, and the settling partner then discharges the debtor, or the creditor sells the debtor a small item for the amount of his share, then discharges him and takes the sale price. Further rulings cover cases where the partner chooses to follow the debtor and the debtor becomes insolvent: the partner has recourse against the settling partner for half of what he received. Other scenarios include purchase with the share, set-off (qisāṣ) situations, deferment (ta'jīl), reduction (ḥaṭṭ), and compromise by one partner in a salam contract. The marginal note clarifies that if the debtor's property is lost, the partner's recourse is not against the specific dirhams received but against the settling partner's liability in kind, as in ḥawālah.

Key Terms
دين مشترك (dayn mushtarak): A debt owed to two or more partners jointly, e.g., price of a single sale or inherited debt.
خيار الشريك (khiyār al-sharīk): The non-settling partner's option to pursue the debtor or the settling partner.
حيلة (ḥīlah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible result while avoiding harm.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or indemnity; here, the settling partner guarantees a portion of the debt to the non-settling partner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two partners jointly own a debt of 1,000, and one partner compromises with the debtor for 600 (a different type), after which the non-settling partner chooses to follow the compromising partner, what are the options of the compromising partner?
A) He must pay the non-settling partner 200 (his share of 600).
B) He may either pay the non-settling partner his share of the settlement (300) or guarantee him 250 (a quarter of the debt).
C) He may only pay the non-settling partner his share of the settlement (300).
D) He must pay the non-settling partner 500 (half of the original debt).

Key Takeaway
The khiyar al-sharik ensures that no partner is unfairly disadvantaged when another partner unilaterally compromises a shared debt.

Conditions for Valid Settlement Among Heirs
Rulings on conditions for valid settlement among co-heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid settlement among co-heirs and identify when a settlement is invalid due to currency exchange rules, debt issues, or lack of knowledge.

Core Idea
Settlement among heirs is valid, but its validity depends on the type of consideration and knowledge of shares; currency exchanges require hand-to-hand transfer.

Settlement (sulh) among co-heirs is a common way to resolve inheritance disputes without formal division. However, classical Hanafi jurists set detailed conditions to ensure fairness and prevent riba. This lesson unpacks the rules from Fatawa Qadikhan, focusing on when the settlement is valid, when it becomes corrupt, and how later-discovered assets are treated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of settlement consideration
Check whether the settlement involves currency (naqdain), commodities (urud), or a mix. The ruling on validity changes with the type.
Currencies require hand-to-hand transfer (taqabud fil-majlis); commodities do not.
2
Determine the knowledge of shares
Assess whether the heirs know the exact share of the settling heir from the type of consideration. If doubt is about existence, it is valid; if about amount, it is corrupt.
This is a key nuance in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the role of the heir in possession
Distinguish between a denying heir (jāḥid) and a acknowledging heir (muqir). For deniers, existing possession suffices; for acknowledgers, a new transfer is needed.
This affects the requirement of taqabud.
4
Check for debts on the estate
If the deceased's debts encumber the entire estate, settlement is invalid unless the heir or a third party guarantees the debt or pays from other funds. If debts do not encumber it, settlement is valid but the debt amount must be set aside.
Debt encumbrance can nullify settlement entirely.
5
Evaluate later-discovered assets
If new assets appear after settlement, the relied-upon view is that they are not included and are distributed among all heirs. This is the mufta bihi position from Fatawa Qadikhan.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the more famous view is exclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ضمان فينوب عن قبض الصلح، وإن كان مقراً غير مانع يشترط تجديد القبض، ولو صالحوه عن النقدين وغيرهما بأحد النقدين لا يصح الصلح ما لم يعلم أن ما أعطوه أكثر من نصيبه من ذلك الجنس إن كانوا متصادقين وإن أنكروا وراثته جاز مطلقاً بشرط التقابض فيما يقابل النقد منه، وإن لم يعلم قدر نصيبه من ذلك الجنس فالصحيح أن الشك إن كان في وجود في التركة جاز الصلح، وإن علم وجود ذلك في التركة لكن لا يدري أن بدل الصلح من حصتها أقل أو أكثر أو مثله فسد؛ كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان ولو كان بدل الصلح عرضاً جاز مطلقاً، ولو كان نقدين جاز مطلقاً بشرط التقابض في المجلس، ولو كان في التركة دين على الناس فأخرجوه ليكون الدين لهم بطل، وإن شرطوا أن يبرأ الغرماء منه صح، ولو كان على الميت دين يحيط بطل الصلح والقسمة إلا أن يضمن الوارث الدين بشرط أن لا يرجع في التركة أو يضمن أجنبي بشرط براءة الميت أو يؤدوا دينه من مال آخر، وإن لم يكن غير الميراث، وإن كان مما ورثوه فعلى قدر ميراثهم. وقيده الخصاف بأن يكون عن إنكار، أما إذا كان عن إقرار فهو بينهم على السواء مطلقاً. وصلح أحدهم عن بعض الأعيان صحيح، وصلح أحدهم عن دعوى أجنبي حقاً في التركة مع غيبة البقية جائز، ويكون متبرعاً في حصة شركائه كالأجنبي. وإن كان صالح على أن يكون حق المدعى له دون غيره فهو جائز، فإن أثبته سلم له وإلا بطل الصلح في حصة الشركاء ويرجع على المدعي بحصة ذلك من البدل والموصى له يمنزلة الوارث فيما قدمناه. وإذا صالحوا أحدهم ثم ظهر للميت دين أو عين لم يعلموها هل يكون داخلاً في الصلح؟ فيه قولان مذكوران في فتاوى قاضيخان قدم أنه لا يكون داخلاً ويكون ذلك الدين والعين بين جميع الورثة وقد ذكر في أول الفتاوى أنه يقدم ما هو الأشهر فكان هو المعتمد. وعلى قول من يقول بالدخول فإن كان الظاهر ديناً فله الصلح كأنه وجد في الابتداء، وإن كان عيناً لا. ولو ادعت الزوجة ميراثها صح الصلح على أقل من نصيبها أو مهرها ولا يطيب لهم إن علموا ذلك، فإن أقامت بينة بطل الصلح . فروع : ادعى أرضاً أنها وقف ولا بينة له فصالحه المنكر لقطع الخصومة جاز ويطيب له
And it is not a condition in the settlement of one of the heirs aforementioned that the specific objects of the estate be known, but if the settlement occurs for one of the two currencies by the other, reciprocity in the session is required. However, if the one who has the rest of the estate is a denier, that transfer suffices because it is a guarantee transfer that substitutes for the settlement transfer; if he is an acknowledgeer not preventing, renewal of the transfer is required. If they settle with him for the two currencies and other things by one of the currencies, the settlement is invalid unless they know that what they gave is more than his share of that type if they are truthful; if they deny his inheritance, it is permissible absolutely with the condition of reciprocity in what corresponds to currency from it. If he does not know the amount of his share of that type, the correct view is that if the doubt is about existence in the estate, the settlement is valid; if they know its existence in the estate but do not know whether the settlement consideration is less, more, or equal to his share, it is corrupt, as in Fatawa Qadikhan. If the settlement consideration is a commodity, it is absolutely permissible; if it is two currencies, it is absolutely permissible with the condition of reciprocity in the session. If there is a debt owed by people in the estate and they take it out to make the debt theirs, it is invalid; if they stipulate that the debtors are released, it is valid. If the deceased had a debt that encircles [the estate], the settlement and division are invalid unless the heir guarantees the debt with the condition that he does not return to the estate, or a third party guarantees with the condition of the deceased's release, or they pay his debt from other wealth. If it is not extensive, the settlement and division are valid, and they raise from it the amount of the debt so that they do not need to rescind the division. It is better not to do that until they pay the debt. If they take out one [heir], his share is divided among the rest equally if what they gave is from their own wealth not the inheritance; if it is from what they inherited, then according to the proportion of their inheritance. Al-Khassaf restricted it to being over denial; if it is over acknowledgment, it is between them equally absolutely. The settlement of one of them over some objects is valid. The settlement of one of them over a claim of a third party for a right in the estate in the absence of the rest is permissible, and he is a volunteer in the share of his partners like a third party. If he settled on condition that the right belongs to the claimant without others, it is permissible; if he proves it, it is surrendered to him, otherwise the settlement becomes void in the partners' share, and he returns to the claimant the share of that from the consideration. The legatee is in the position of the heir in what we have presented. If they settle with one of them, then a debt or object of the deceased appears that they did not know of, is it included in the settlement? There are two opinions mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan; the one given is that it is not included, and that debt or object is among all the heirs. And it was mentioned at the beginning of the Fatawa that the more famous is given preference, so it is the relied-upon view. According to the one who says inclusion, if the apparent is a debt, he has the settlement as if it were found initially; if it is an object, not. If the wife claims her inheritance, settlement for less than her share or her dower is valid, and it is not lawful for them if they know that; if she establishes evidence, the settlement is void. Branches: If someone claims that land is waqf without evidence, and the denier settles with him to end the litigation, it is permissible and it is lawful for him.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a dense legal text from Fatawa Qadikhan on the rules of settlement (sulh) among co-heirs regarding inheritance. It begins by stating that knowledge of the specific items of the estate is not a condition for the validity of settlement. However, if the settlement involves exchanging one currency for another, hand-to-hand transfer (qabd) in the session is required. The text then distinguishes between a denying heir (who has possession and is denying the claim) and an acknowledging heir: for the denier, existing possession suffices for transfer; for the acknowledger, a new transfer is needed. If settlement is for multiple types including currency, it must be known that the consideration is more than the heir's share from that type, otherwise invalid. The correct view is that if there is doubt about the existence of that type in the estate, settlement is valid; but if existence is certain but the amount is unknown, it is invalid. Commodities as consideration are always valid, while two currencies require hand-to-hand transfer. If the estate includes debts on others, taking those debts for themselves invalidates the settlement; but stipulating release of the debtors is valid. If the deceased's debts encumber the estate completely, settlement and division are invalid unless the heir or a third party guarantees the debt or they pay from other funds. If debts do not encumber it, settlement is valid, and they should set aside the debt amount. When one heir is bought out, his share is divided among the others equally if they paid from their own wealth, or proportionally if from inheritance. Al-Khassaf restricts this to cases of denial; if it's acknowledgment, equal division applies. Settlement for part of the estate is valid, as is settlement with a third party claimant in the absence of other heirs—the settling heir is a volunteer. If a claim is established, the settlement stands; if not, it becomes void for the partners' shares. The legatee is like an heir. If unknown assets appear later, the view in Fatawa Qadikhan is that they are not included in the earlier settlement and are distributed among all heirs. The wife can settle for less than her inheritance, but if she proves her right, the settlement becomes void. The final branch: settling a claim of waqf without evidence, if done to end litigation, is permissible and lawful for the settlement taker.

Key Terms
صلح (sulh): A settlement or compromise between parties to end a dispute, often involving a transfer of property.
النقدين (al-naqdain): The two currencies: gold and silver (dinar and dirham).
التقابض في المجلس (al-taqabud fi al-majlis): The hand-to-hand transfer of currency in the same session, required to make the exchange valid and avoid riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If co-heirs settle with one heir using a commodity, what is the ruling?
A) Invalid because shares must be known exactly.
B) Valid without any conditions.
C) Valid only if the commodity is of equal value.
D) Invalid unless hand-to-hand transfer occurs.

Key Takeaway
Settlement among heirs is a flexible instrument, but its validity hinges on the nature of the consideration and the clarity of the share amount when currency is involved.

6 min
Definition and Rulings of Wadi'a (Deposit)
Defining wadi'a, its pillars, and examples of acceptance by indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define wadi'a, identify its pillars (ijab and qabul), and distinguish between explicit and implicit forms of offer and acceptance in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A deposit is a trust, not a guarantee; silence can speak acceptance.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational contract of wadi'a — the deposit. Derived from the root meaning 'to leave', wadi'a is a trust-based relationship where the depositary holds property without liability unless negligent. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the pillars of this contract and the nuanced ways offer and acceptance can be expressed, including by action or silence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal nature of wadi'a
Determine that wadi'a is an amanah (trust) and not a guarantee. Recognize that liability only arises from negligence, not from mere custody.
2
Analyze the rukn (pillar) of the contract
The rukn consists of two parts: ijab (offer) and qabul (acceptance). Both are essential for a valid deposit.
3
Categorize the modes of ijab
Ijab can be explicit (sarih) by words like 'I deposit with you', metaphorical (kinayah) like 'give me' implying request for custody, or by action (fi'l) such as placing an item before someone without words.
Examples from the text: saying 'give me' (kinayah), placing clothes in front of bath attendant (action).
4
Examine the modes of qabul
Qabul can be explicit by words or by indication (dalalah), including silence when the item is placed before the depositary and he does not object. Silence implies acceptance in Hanafi fiqh.
The bathhouse example: if the attendant is present and silent, he is not a depositary; if absent, his role implies acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوديعة الإيداع تسليط الغير على حفظ ماله والوديعة ما تترك عند الأمين وهي أمانة فلا ماله) من لا خفاء في اشتراكها مع ما قبلها في الحكم وهو الأمانة . وهي في اللغة مشتقة الودع وهو الترك، وفي الشريعة ما ذكره المصنف قوله : (الإيداع هو تسليط الغير على حفظ يعني صرع صريحاً أو دلالة وإنما قلنا أو دلالة لأن المنقول في المحيط أنه لو انفتق زق رجل فأخذه رجل ثم تركه ولم يكن المالك حاضراً يضمن لأنه لما أخذه فقد التزم حفظه دلالة وإن لم يأخذه ولم يذق منه لا يضمن، وإن كان المالك حاضراً لم يضمن في الوجهين قوله : (والوديعة ما تترك عند الأمين وركنها الإيجاب قولاً صريحاً أو كناية أو فعلاً والقبول من المودع صريحاً أو دلالة في حق وجوب الحفظ وإنما قلنا صريحاً أو كناية ليشمل ما لو قال الرجل أعطني أو قال لرجل في يده ثوب أعطنيه فقال أعطيتك فهذا على الوديعة؛ نص عليه في المحيط. لأن الإعطاء يحتمل الهبة والوديعة والوديعة أدنى وهو متيقن فصار كناية. وإنما قلنا في الإيجاب أو فعلاً ليشمل ما لو وضع ثوبه بين يدي رجل ولم يقل شيئاً فهو إيداع. وإنما قلنا في القبول أو دلالة ليشمل سكوته عند وضعه بين يديه فإنه قبول دلالة حتى لو قال لا أقبل لا يكون مودعاً لأن الدلالة لم توجد ولهذا قال في الخلاصة : لو وضع كتابه عند قوم فذهبوا وتركوه ضمنوا إذا ضاع وإن قاموا واحداً بعد واحد ضمن الأخير لأنه تعين للحفظ فتعين للضمان ا هـ . ولهذا إذا وضع ثيابه في الحمام بمرأى من الثيابي كان إيداعاً وإن لم يتكلم، ولا يكون الحمامي مودعاً ما دام الثيابي حاضراً فإن كان غائباً فالحمامي مودع، وكذلك إذا قال لصاحب الخان أين أربطها فقال هناك كان إيداعاً ؛ كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان .
Book of Deposit (Wadi'a). Deposition (al-ida') is authorizing another to preserve one's property, and the deposit (al-wadi'a) is what is left with a trustworthy person. It is a trust (amanah), so no liability... It is evident that it shares with the preceding [chapter] in the ruling, which is amanah. Linguistically, it is derived from 'al-wada'a' meaning leaving. In Shari'ah, it is what the author mentioned. His statement: 'Deposition is authorizing another to preserve his property, meaning explicitly or by indication.' We said 'or by indication' because it is related in al-Muhit that if a man's wineskin burst and a man took it and then left it while the owner was not present, he is liable because by taking it he implicitly undertook its custody. If he did not take it and did not take from it, he is not liable. If the owner was present, he is not liable in both cases. His statement: 'The deposit is what is left with a trustworthy person, and its pillar (rukn) is the offer (ijab) explicitly by word, by metaphor, or by action, and the acceptance (qabul) from the depositary (muda') explicitly or by indication regarding the obligation of custody.' We said 'explicitly or by metaphor' to include if a man said 'give me' or said to a man in whose hand there is a garment 'give it to me' and he said 'I gave you'—this is a deposit, as stated in al-Muhit, because 'giving' could mean gift or deposit, and deposit is lesser and certain, so it becomes a metaphor. We said in the offer 'or by action' to include if he placed his garment before a man and said nothing—it is a deposit. We said in acceptance 'or by indication' to include his silence when it is placed before him—it is acceptance by indication, such that if he said 'I do not accept' he is not a depositary because the indication did not occur. For this reason, it is said in al-Khulasah: if he placed his book with a group and they left and abandoned it, they are liable if it is lost; and if they left one after another, the last one is liable because he became specified for custody, thus specified for liability. End. For this reason, if he placed his clothes in the bathroom in the sight of the bathkeeper, it is a deposit even if he did not speak, and the bathkeeper is not a depositary as long as the bathkeeper is present; if he is absent, the bathkeeper is a depositary. Similarly, if he said to the innkeeper 'where shall I tie it?' and he said 'there', it is a deposit, as in Fatawa Qadikhan.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the rulings of wadi'a (deposit). It begins by stating that wadi'a is an amanah (trust), not a guarantee. The rukn (pillar) consists of ijab (offer) and qabul (acceptance). Ijab can be explicit (by words like 'I leave this with you'), by kinayah (metaphor, e.g., 'give me' which implies request for custody), or by action (e.g., placing an item before someone silently). Qabul can be explicit or by indication (e.g., silence when the item is placed). The text gives examples: if a man says 'give me' and the other gives, it is deemed a deposit because the default is trust, not ownership. If someone takes a burst wineskin without the owner's presence, he becomes liable because his action implies acceptance of custody. In a bathhouse, if the owner places clothes in view of the attendant, it is a deposit; the attendant is not liable if present (because he might not have accepted), but if absent, the attendant becomes the depositary by virtue of his role. The key takeaway is that the relationship is based on trust, and liability only arises if the depositary acts negligently or explicitly refuses.

Key Terms
وديعة (wadi'a): Property left with a trustworthy person for safekeeping; a deposit.
إيداع (ida'): The act of depositing; authorizing another to preserve one's property.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; property held without liability for loss unless negligence is proven.
مستودع (mustawda'): The depositary; the person entrusted with the deposit.
صريح (sarih): Explicit statement directly expressing the intended meaning.
كناية (kinayah): A metaphorical or indirect expression that implies the intended meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person places his clothes in the bathroom in the sight of the bathkeeper without speaking, and the bathkeeper remains silent, what is the ruling?
A) It is not a deposit because there was no verbal offer or acceptance.
B) It is a deposit, and the bathkeeper is immediately liable for loss.
C) It is a deposit if the bathkeeper is absent; if present, he is not a depositary.
D) It is a deposit, and the bathkeeper becomes the depositary only if he verbally accepts.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a deposit (wadi'a) is a trust contract formed by offer and acceptance, which can be explicit or implicit through action or silence.
