Two Depositors: Depositary Cannot Deliver to One Alone
Intra-Hanafi dispute on depositary's liability for premature delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions within the Hanafi school regarding a depositary's liability when delivering a portion of a joint deposit to one depositor before the others are present, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Delivering part of a joint deposit to one depositor alone triggers liability by qiyas, but istihsan exempts the depositary, and this is the chosen opinion.

When two or more people jointly deposit an item with a trusted person, may the depositary give part of it to one of them before the others are present? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rule and the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply istihsan in trustee situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the rule
The depositary delivers a portion of a joint deposit to one depositor without the others present. The base rule from Kanz al-Daqa'iq is that this is not permissible.
The rule applies to both fungibles (mithli) and valuables (qimi).
2
Distinguish the qiyas position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: by qiyas on joint debt, the depositary is liable because he does not own the item. Just as a debtor pays his own share, a depositary is a trustee, not an owner, so delivery is a transgression.
Key difference: in debt, the debtor pays his own obligation; in deposit, the depositary holds another's property.
3
Understand the istihsan position
Abu Yusuf: by istihsan, the depositary is not liable. The instruction 'do not give until we gather' is a condition that may be waived by implication, since delivery will eventually happen.
Istihsan overrides strict analogy to avoid hardship.
4
Note the corollaries
Even a judge cannot compel the depositary to give a share to one alone. If the depositary gives despite the prohibition, it is not a valid partition; if the rest is lost, the other depositor can claim from the taker.
The depositary is not liable for the act itself, but the taker bears responsibility for the other's share.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text states 'fakana al-mukhtar' – the chosen opinion is Abu Yusuf's istihsan, i.e., no liability.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو أودعا شيئاً لم يدفع المودع إلى أحدهما حظه حتى يعني في غيبة صاحبه أطلقه فشمل ذوات الأمثال والقيم وخلافهما في الأول قياساً على الدين المشترك. وفرق أبو حنيفة بينهما بأن المودع لا يملك القسمة بينهما فكان تعدياً على ملك الغير، وفي الدين يطالبه بتسليم حقه إذ الديون تقضى بأمثالها فكان تصرفاً في مال نفسه. وأشار بقوله «لم يدفع إلى أنه لا يجوز ذلك حتى لو خاصمه إلى القاضي لم يأمره بدفع نصيبه إليه في قول أبي حنيفة، وإلى أنه لو دفع إليه لا يكون قسمة اتفاقاً . حتى لو هلك الباقي رجع صاحبه على الآخذ بحصته، وإلى أن لأحدهما أن يأخذ حصته منها إذا ظفر بها، وإلى أنه لو دفع وارتكب الممنوع لا يضمن وفي فتاوى قاضيخان ما يفيده ولفظه : ثلاثة أودعوا . رجلاً مالاً وقالوا لا تدفع المال إلى أحد منا حتى نجتمع فدفع نصيب أحدهم قال محمد في القياس يكون ضامناً وبه قال أبو حنيفة. وفي الاستحسان لا يضمن وهو قول أبي يوسف الضمان الاستحسان فكان المختار
His statement: (And if they deposit something, the depositary shall not give to one of them his share until) meaning in the absence of his companion; he made it absolute, so it includes fungibles and valuables and their opposites. In the former, by analogy to joint debt. And Abu Hanifa distinguished between them: because the depositary does not have the right of division between them, so it would be a transgression against the property of another; whereas in debt, he demands delivery of his right, because debts are paid by their like, so it is a disposal of his own property. And he indicated by his statement 'shall not give' that this is not permissible, even if he brings him to the judge, the judge does not order him to give his share to him in the opinion of Abu Hanifa; and that if he gives it, it is not a valid division by agreement; so if the remainder perishes, the other owner has recourse against the taker for his share; and that one of them may take his share if he finds it; and that if he gives and commits the prohibited, he is not liable. And in Fatawa Qadikhan, something that indicates it, and its wording: Three men deposited property with a man and said 'Do not give the property to any one of us until we all gather', then he gave the share of one of them. Muhammad said: by analogy, he is liable, and Abu Hanifa agreed. By istihsan, he is not liable, which is the saying of Abu Yusuf. So the chosen (mukhtar) is istihsan.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rule when two (or more) people jointly deposit an item with a single depositary. According to the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the depositary must not give any portion to one of the depositors until the other is present. The commentator explains that this applies whether the deposit is fungible (mithli) or non-fungible (qimi), analogizing to joint debt. However, Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in the case of a deposit, the depositary does not own the item, so delivering a portion to one is a transgression; in a debt, the debtor can pay his share in fungibles. The commentary then elaborates several corollaries: even a judge cannot compel the depositary to give a share to one; if he does give, it is not a valid partition, and if the rest is lost, the other depositor can claim from the taker; the depositary is not liable if he commits the prohibited act? Actually, there is a dispute: in Fatawa Qadikhan, a case of three depositors: by qiyas (analogy) the depositary is liable if he gives to one prematurely, but by istihsan (juristic preference) he is not liable, and this is the chosen view (mukhtar). The passage thus presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (by qiyas) say liable; Abu Yusuf (by istihsan) says not liable. The mufta bihi is the istihsan view. The key distinction is that the depositary's act is a violation of instructions, but istihsan considers that he was fulfilling the intention of the depositors by delivering to one, as they eventually will take.

Key Terms
وديعة مشتركة (wadi'ah mushtarakah): a deposit owned jointly by two or more persons.
استحسان (istihsan): juristic preference over qiyas due to equity or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, if the depositary gives the share to one depositor before the other arrives, he is not liable. What is the basis?
A) Qiyas
B) Istihsan
C) Ijma
D) Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on joint deposits is that the depositary is not liable if he delivers a portion to one depositor before the others are present, by istihsan.

Two Depositaries: Division of Custody and Liability
Ruling on when a deposit is given to two depositaries and how they handle custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling on divisible deposits given to two depositaries, explain the Sahibayn's opposing view, and apply the reasoning to similar joint roles.

Core Idea
If two depositaries divide a divisible deposit, each is trustee of his half; transferring to the other makes the giver liable.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a scenario where a single deposit is entrusted to two individuals. The key question: can one depositary take full custody with the other's permission? Abu Hanifa insists on division if the item is divisible, while his two companions allow delegation. The ruling extends to other joint roles like two pledgees or two agents.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from Abu Hanifa as presented in the matn: for a divisible deposit, the two depositaries must divide it and each keep his half. If one gives his portion to the other, the giver becomes liable.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Note the opposing opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn): they allow one depositary to keep the entire deposit with the other's permission, without liability.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand their reasoning: the depositor was satisfied with the trustworthiness of each individual; thus, if both agree, the transfer is permissible.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain Abu Hanifa's counter-argument: the depositor's satisfaction was for joint custody, not singular custody. Thus, transferring one's share without the depositor's consent is a transgression.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if the deposit is lost after transfer, according to Abu Hanifa the giver is liable; according to Sahibayn, neither is liable if there was permission.
6
Apply qiyas to similar joint roles
Recognize that the same ruling applies to two pledgees, two sendees, two executors, two arbiters in pledge, and two agents for purchase: if one hands over to the other, the giver is liable.
This is based on the shared illa of joint responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن أودع رجل عند رجلين مما يقسم اقتسماه وحفظ كل نصفه ولو دفع إلى الآخر ضمن بخلاف ما لا يقسم) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا لأحدهما أن يحفظ بإذن الآخر مطلقاً لأنه رضي بأمانتهما، وله إنما رضي بحفظهما لا بحفظ أحدهما . قيد بضمان الدافع لأن القابض لا ضمان عليه لأنه مودع المودع . وقيد بقوله «اقتسماه» لأن فيما يقسم لو أبيا القسمة وأودعاه فهلك ضمناه التركهما ما التزاماه، وكذلك الجواب في المرتهنين والمستبضعين والوصيين والعدلين في الرهن والوكيلين بالشراء إذا سلم أحدهما إلى الآخر، وإذا لم يكن لهما القسمة فيما لا يقسم كان
His statement: (If a man deposits something with two men which is divisible, they divide it and each keeps half; and if one gives it to the other, he is liable; unlike what is not divisible.) And this is according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: one of them may keep it with the permission of the other absolutely, because the depositor was satisfied with their trustworthiness; but he only was satisfied with their joint custody, not with one alone. He restricted by the liability of the giver because the receiver is not liable, as he is the depositary of the depositary. And he restricted by his statement 'they divide it' because in divisible items, if they refuse to divide and then deposit it and it perishes, they are liable for what they undertook. Similarly, the ruling in the case of two pledgees, two sendees, two executors, two arbiters in pledge, and two agents for purchase, if one hands over to the other. And if division is not possible for them in what is not divisible, then...
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a single deposit is given to two depositaries. The matn states: if the item is divisible (like grain, money), they should split it and each keep half; if one gives his half to the other (i.e., entrusts the other with his portion), the giver becomes liable (because he delegated custody without permission). If the item is not divisible (like a single animal), they must keep it jointly. Abu Hanifa holds this position. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that one of them may keep the entire deposit with the other's permission, because the depositor agreed to their amanah (trustworthiness) collectively, but the depositor's consent is for both of them jointly, not for one alone without proper authorization. The commentator clarifies that the liability falls on the giver (the one who transfers), not the receiver, because the receiver is considered a sub-depositary (mudi' al-mudi') and is not liable unless he exceeds. The ruling is then extended to similar cases: two pledgees (murtahinayn), two sendees (mustabdi'ayn), two executors (wasiyayn), two arbiters in pledge (adlayn fi al-rahn), and two agents for purchase (wakilayn bil-shira'). In all these, if one transfers his share to the other without the other's consent (or without proper division), the giver is liable. The passage ends abruptly, but the point is clear: the default is joint responsibility.

Key Terms
مُودِع (mudi'): depositary: the person who receives the deposit for safekeeping.
قسمة (qismah): division of a joint property among co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a divisible deposit is given to two depositaries and one gives his portion to the other, what is the ruling?
A) The giver becomes liable
B) The receiver becomes liable
C) Both become liable
D) Neither is liable

Key Takeaway
When a divisible deposit is entrusted to two depositaries, Abu Hanifa requires physical division; transferring one's share to the other makes the giver liable, and this ruling extends by qiyas to all joint trustees.

Liability of the Custodian of a Usurper vs. Original Custodian
Expansion of a ruling on liability of deposit-takers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds the custodian of a usurper liable while the custodian of the original custodian is not liable before separation, and apply the underlying illa to related chains of possession.

Core Idea
A possessor without owner's permission at any stage is liable; a possessor with permission is not until he relinquishes control.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq sharpens a crucial distinction in Hanafi liability law: not every subsequent holder of a deposit is automatically liable. The difference hinges on whether the original possessor had any owner's permission. Abu Hanifa explains why the custodian of a usurper must compensate the owner, while the custodian of the original custodian does not, until he physically separates from the property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between the custodian of a usurper (mudi' al-ghasib) and the custodian of the original custodian (mudi' al-mudi').
The ruling for each is different according to Abu Hanifa.
2
State the ruling for each
The custodian of a usurper is liable (damān); the custodian of the original custodian is not liable until he separates from the deposit.
Liability means compensation to the owner.
3
Understand the illa (effective cause)
The usurper has no owner's permission at all (initially and perpetually), so any possession derived from him is based on invalid title. The original custodian has initial permission, so his possession is valid until he relinquishes it.
The illa is 'lack of owner's permission in the chain of possession'.
4
Apply the qiyas
The custodian of a usurper is analogous to the usurper himself in terms of liability because both possess without owner's permission. The original custodian's deputy is not analogous because the original custodian had permission.
The qiyas panel in the toolbox formalizes this.
5
Extend to further chains
The text states that if the custodian of a usurper is liable, then the usurper of the usurper and the buyer from him are liable a fortiori (bil-awla).
This shows the principle applies recursively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وضمن مودع الغاصب لا مودع المودع والفرق بينهما على قول أبي حنيفة أن غاصب لعدم إذن المالك ابتداء وبقاء وفي الثاني ليس بغاصب لأنه لا يضمن المودع بمجرد الدفع ما لم يفارقه، وإذا ضمن مودع الغاصب رجع على الغاصب مطلقاً علم أنه غاصب أو لا. وإذا ضمن مودع الغاصب ضمن غاصب الغاصب والمشتري منه بالأولى، وقد تقدم في المضاربة أن المضارب لو دفع المال مضاربة بلا إذن لا يضمن واحد منهما قبل عمل الثاني
His words: (And the custodian of the usurper is liable, not the custodian of the custodian. The difference between them according to Abu Hanifa is that the usurper is a usurper due to lack of the owner's permission initially and perpetually, while in the second he is not a usurper because the custodian is not liable merely by handing over as long as he does not separate from it. And if the custodian of the usurper becomes liable, he has recourse against the usurper absolutely, whether he knew he was a usurper or not. And if the custodian of the usurper becomes liable, then the usurper of the usurper and the buyer from him are liable a fortiori. And it has preceded in Mudarabah that if the mudarib gives the capital as a mudarabah without permission, neither is liable before the work of the second.)
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability of a person who receives a deposit from a usurper (ghasib) versus someone who receives it from the original depositor (mawda'). The key distinction: the usurper has no owner's permission at all, so any act based on his possession is invalid. Thus, if a person takes a deposit from a usurper, he is liable to the owner because he is in a chain of invalid possession. However, if the original custodian hands the deposit to another person, he is not automatically liable; he only becomes liable if he separates from the item (i.e., gives it completely). According to Abu Hanifa, the custodian of the usurper is liable, and then he can claim reimbursement from the usurper. This ruling also applies to subsequent persons in the chain.

Key Terms
الغاصب (al-ghasib): A usurper: one who takes property without owner's permission in a manner that is legally prohibited.
مودع الغاصب (mudi' al-ghasib): The custodian of the usurper: one who receives a deposit from the usurper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the custodian of a usurper liable while the custodian of the original custodian is not?
A) Because the usurper is a sinner.
B) Because the usurper’s possession lacks owner’s permission entirely, while the original custodian has initial permission.
C) Because the custodian of the usurper is also a usurper.
D) Because the original custodian is always liable.

Key Takeaway
The liability of a subsequent custodian depends on whether the chain of possession originates from a usurper (no permission) or a permitted custodian (with permission).

Evaluating the Muhtar Position in Custodian's Liability
Critical refinement on the muhtar position regarding custodian's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the internal Hanafi dispute over the muhtar position regarding custodian's liability and identify which view is preferred by later authorities.

Core Idea
The muhtar position is not always the Imam's own view; later scholars may prefer another based on istihsan and consensus.

In this passage, we see a critical refinement of the muhtar position. Al-Marqinani had claimed a view is muhtar, but Al-Maqdisi challenges this, citing that the majority of texts follow Imam Abu Hanifa. This illustrates the dynamic nature of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim
What did Al-Marqinani state? He claimed 'فكان هو المختار' (so it is the chosen one) regarding the custodian's liability.
2
Locate the objection
Al-Maqdisi objects: How can it be the chosen one when other texts follow the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa)?
3
Cite supporting authorities
Al-Nasafi, Al-Mahbubi, and Sadr al-Shari'ah chose the Imam's view (no liability). Thus, the majority of later scholars favor no liability.
4
Analyze the basis of the dispute
Some argue the muhtar is based on istihsan, but the majority of leading imams and texts agree on the opposite. Which basis is stronger?
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the custodian is liable, he pays compensation; if not liable, he does not. The note suggests the mufta bihi is no liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فكان هو المختار) تعقبه المقدسي فقال : كيف يكون هو المختار أن مع سائر المتون على قول الإمام؟ وقال الشيخ قاسم: اختار النسفي قول الإمام والمحبوبي وصدر الشريعة وقال المقدسي : وقول بعضهم عدم الضمان هو المختار مستدلاً بكونه الاستحسان مخالف لما عليه الأئمة الأعيان بل غالب المتون عليه متفقون. حموي كذا في حاشية أبي السعود.
His words: (So it was the chosen one). Al-Maqdisi criticized him and said: How can it be the chosen one when the other texts follow the statement of the Imam? And Shaykh Qasim said: Al-Nasafi chose the statement of the Imam, and al-Mahbubi and Sadr al-Shari'ah. And al-Maqdisi said: And the statement of some that there is no liability is the chosen one, arguing that it is istihsan, contrary to what the leading imams are upon, rather the majority of texts agree on it. Hamawi: as in the hashiah of Abu al-Su'ud.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This is a critical note (hashiyah) discussing which position is 'muhtar' (preferred) regarding the liability of the custodian in a specific issue (likely from the earlier lesson about the custodian of the usurper or similar). The commentator Al-Marqinani (author of al-Hidayah) had stated 'فكان هو المختار' (so it is the chosen one). Al-Maqdisi objected: How can this be the chosen one when the majority of other texts follow the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa? He cites Shaykh Qasim saying that Al-Nasafi, Al-Mahbubi, and Sadr al-Shari'ah chose Abu Hanifa's view, which is that there is no liability. Some others say the chosen view is that there is no liability, based on istihsan. The note concludes that al-Hamawi reports this from the hashiah of Abu al-Su'ud. This shows internal Hanafi disagreement on which ruling is relied upon.

Key Terms
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred legal position among differing opinions within the Hanafi school.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that overrides qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the note, which scholars chose the view of no liability for the custodian?
A) Al-Maqdisi and Al-Marqinani.
B) Al-Nasafi, Al-Mahbubi, and Sadr al-Shari'ah.
C) Al-Hamawi and Abu al-Su'ud.
D) Only Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the muhtar position is not fixed; later scholars may prefer a different view based on consensus and istihsan, as seen in the dispute over custodian's liability.

Two Claimants to a Deposit: Oath and Distribution
Procedure when two men claim a deposit and the custodian denies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi procedure when two claimants dispute a deposit and the custodian denies, including the role of nukul (refusal of oath) and distribution rules.

Core Idea
Refusal of oath (nukul) can lead to judgment against the refuser, but the judge may delay to allow oath for another claimant.

This lesson unpacks a detailed procedural ruling from Al-Bahr al-Raiq on a scenario where a custodian holds a thousand dirhams and two men each claim it was their deposit. The custodian denies both. How does the judge resolve this? The answer involves oaths, refusal of oaths (nukul), and a compensation mechanism. Understanding this clarifies the Hanafi approach to evidence and judgment in property disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and initial claim
Two men each claim that a specific sum (a thousand dirhams) held by the custodian is their own deposit. The custodian denies both deposits.
This is a dispute over ownership of a physical asset held by a third party.
2
Understand the role of oaths
The custodian may be required to swear an oath denying the deposit. If he refuses (nukul) for a claimant, that refusal is treated as evidence against him.
Nukul is not as strong as confession but can lead to judgment.
3
Analyze the sequence of oaths and nukul
The judge may start with any claimant, but lots is recommended. If the custodian swears for one claimant and refuses for the other, judgment goes to the one for whom he refused. If he refuses for the first and then swears for the second, the first gets the entire sum (because the second's claim is negated).
The order matters: the judge can delay judgment after nukul to allow another oath.
4
Determine the distribution when both refuse
If the custodian refuses oath for both, both claimants are considered entitled: the original sum is divided equally, and the custodian must pay another thousand to be divided between them (compensation for the disputed portion).
This is a unique Hanafi rule – the custodian bears a penalty for his refusal.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability
Abu Yusuf holds that if a judge rules in favor of one claimant without following the procedure, the custodian is not liable; Muhammad says he is liable. The relied-upon view is the detailed procedure as described.
This shows the range of opinion within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (معه ألف فادعى رجلان كل أنه له أودعه اياه فنكل لهما فالألف لهما وغرم ألفاً آخر بينهما) أشار بقوله نكل إلى أن المودع يحلف إذا أنكر الإيداع كما يحلف إذا ادعى ردها أو هلاكها إما لنفي التهمة أو لإنكاره الضمان ولو حلف لا يثبت الرد بيمينه حتى لا يضمن لو ادعى الرد عليه وحلف؛ كذا في المبسوط وإلى أنه لو حلف لا شيء لهما عليه وإلى أنه لو حلف لأحدهما ونكل للآخر قضى به لمن نكل له فقط وإلى أن للقاضي أن يبدأ لأيهما شاء بالتحليف والأولى القرعة، وإلى أنه لو نكل للأول يحلف للثاني ولا يقضى بالنكول بخلاف ما إذا أقر لأحدهما لأن الإقرار حجة بنفسه فيقضي به. أما النكول فإنما يصير حجة عند القضاء فجاز أن يؤخره ليحلف للثاني فينكشف وجه القضاء فإن حلف للثاني فالكل للأول، وإن نكل فهي بينهما، فإن قضى للأول حين نكل قبل أن يحلف للثاني لا ينفذ قضاؤه خلافاً للخصاف. وذكر الألف في الكتاب ليس احترازاً كما أن العبد في كلام الخصاف ليس احترازياً. وفي التحليف للثاني يقول بالله ما هذه العين له ولا قيمتها لأنه لما أقر بها للأول ثبت الحق فيها له فلا يفيد إقراره بها للثاني، فلو اقتصر على الأول كان صادقاً. قيد المصنف بهذه الصورة لأنه لو أقر بها لإنسان ثم قال بل هي لهذا اختص بها الأول وضمن للآخر قيمتها إن دفعها بغير قضاء، وإن كان بقضاء لا يكون ضامناً عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد . ولو قال أودعنيها أحدكما ولا أدري أيكما فإن اصطلحا على أخذها بينهما فلهما ذلك ولا ضمان عليه وليس له الامتناع من التسليم بعد الصلح وإلا وادعاها كل وأراد أخذها ليس له ذلك لأن المقر له مجهول ولكل أن يستحلفه، فإن حلف قطع دعواهما، وإن نكل فكمسألة الكتاب وكذا لو قال علي ألف ألف لهذا أو لهذا ا هـ . والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
His words: (He has a thousand [dirhams] and two men each claim that it is his which he deposited with him, and he refused oath for both, so the thousand is for both and he pays another thousand between them.) He indicated by his word 'refused oath' that the depositor takes an oath if he denies the deposit, just as he takes an oath if he claims its return or its loss, either to negate suspicion or to deny liability. And if he takes an oath, the return is not established by his oath, so he is not liable if he claimed return and took oath; as in al-Mabsut. And that if he takes an oath, nothing is due to them. And that if he takes an oath for one and refuses oath for the other, judgment is given to the one for whom he refused. And that the judge may begin with whichever he wishes, and the preferred method is lots. And that if he refuses oath for the first, then takes oath for the second, judgment is not given by nukul, unlike if he confessed to one, because confession is a proof in itself, so judgment is given by it. As for nukul, it only becomes a proof upon judgment, so it is permissible to delay it to take oath for the second to reveal the judgment; if he takes oath for the second, all is for the first; if he refuses, it is between them. If he judged for the first at the moment of nukul before taking oath for the second, his judgment is not executed, contrary to al-Khassaf. And mentioning 'thousand' in the book is not restrictive, just as 'slave' in the words of al-Khassaf is not restrictive. And in the oath for the second, he says: 'By Allah, this physical object is not his, nor its value,' because when he confessed it to the first, the right in it became established for him, so his confession of it to the second is not beneficial. So if he limited to the first, he is truthful. The author restricted to this picture because if he confessed it to someone and then said 'rather it is to this one,' the first gets it specifically and he guarantees its value to the other if he gives it without judgment; if it was by judgment, he is not liable according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. And if he said: 'One of you deposited it with me, and I do not know which,' then if they agree to take it between them, that is for them and there is no liability on him; he is not prevented from delivering after the settlement. Otherwise, each claims it and wants to take it, he is not permitted because the confesee is unknown, and each may ask him to take an oath. If he takes an oath, their claims are cut; if he refuses oath, it is like the case of the book. Similarly, if he said: 'I owe a thousand, either to this one or to that one.' End. And Allah Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage explains a complex legal scenario: a custodian has a thousand dirhams, and two men each claim that they deposited it with him. The custodian denies both claims. If he refuses to take an oath (nukul) for both, then the sum is divided between the two claimants, and he must also pay another thousand dirhams to be divided between them (as a penalty for his refusal? Actually the text says 'so the thousand is for both and he pays another thousand between them' – this is because he admitted by his nukul that the sum belongs to them, but since they both claim it, it becomes like a joint property and he must compensate for the disputed portion? The commentary clarifies procedural details: the custodian's oath is required when he denies the deposit. If he takes an oath for one and refuses for the other, the one for whom he refused wins. The judge may decide the order of oaths, but lots is recommended. If the custodian refuses for the first, then swears for the second, judgment is not immediate; the oath for the second clarifies the situation. If he swears for the second, the first claimant gets the whole sum? Actually the text says 'فالكل للأول' meaning if he takes oath for the second, then the first gets all? Wait: 'فإن حلف للثاني فالكل للأول' – if he (the custodian) takes oath for the second, then all is for the first? That seems contradictory. Actually the commentary: if he refuses for the first and then swears for the second, the implication is that the second's claim is false, so the first's claim stands, and he gets the whole thousand. But then if he refuses for both, it is divided. The passage also discusses confessions and judgments. This is a detailed procedural ruling for disputes over deposits.

Key Terms
نكل (nakala): Refused to take an oath; nukul (the act of refusing an oath) is a legal indication that the refuse admits the claim.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Confession; admission of a right against oneself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a custodian with a thousand dirhams denies deposit claims from two men, and he refuses oath for both, what is the ruling?
A) The thousand is returned to the custodian.
B) The thousand is divided equally between the two claimants, and the custodian must pay an additional thousand to be divided.
C) Each claimant takes the whole thousand.
D) The custodian is imprisoned until he confesses.

Key Takeaway
In a deposit dispute with two claimants, the custodian's refusal to take an oath (nukul) can lead to division of the deposit plus a penalty, but the judge must carefully sequence oaths to avoid premature judgment.

The Hanafi Definition of 'Ariyah: Ownership of Usufruct
Defines 'ariyah and discusses its linguistic origins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'ariyah and explain its key components: tamlik, manafi', bi-ghayr 'iwad.

Core Idea
'Ariyah is a transfer of ownership of usufruct, not mere permission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the discussion of 'ariyah by providing its legal definition. The author carefully distinguishes it from similar contracts and establishes it as a transfer (tamlik) rather than mere permission (ibaha), setting the stage for all subsequent rulings on liability, expenses, and the borrower's rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
The text defines 'ariyah as 'tamlik al-manafi' bi-ghayr 'iwad'. Write down these three components.
Tamlik = ownership transfer; manafi' = usufructs; 'iwad = compensation.
2
Understand each component
Explain what tamlik, manafi', and 'iwad mean in fiqh. Tamlik indicates a transfer of ownership, manafi' are the uses/benefits of an object, and 'iwad is compensation.
This definition distinguishes 'ariyah from a gift (tamlik al-'ayn) and a loan of money (qard).
3
Explore the etymology
The author discusses linguistic origins from 'ar (shame) or 'arah (i'arah) or ta'awur (alternation). Understand why the preferred derivation is from 'arah (i'arah), as Allah himself engaged in borrowing (ist'ara).
The linguistic discussion is not essential for the legal ruling but shows careful scholarship.
4
Distinguish from wadi'ah
The text notes that 'ariyah involves tamlik, unlike wadi'ah which is pure trust (amana) without ownership transfer. Both are amana, but only 'ariyah grants ownership of usufruct.
This distinction clarifies the unique nature of 'ariyah.
5
Connect to the refutation
Note that this definition directly contradicts al-Karkhi's view of ibaha. The definition itself is the foundation for refuting that view.
The author immediately uses the definition to set up the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العارية

هي تمليك المنفعة بلا عوض وتصح باعرتك وأطعمتك أرضي ومنحتك ثوبي

كتاب العارية

وفي أخرها عن الوديعة لأن فيها تمليكاً وإن اشتركا في الأمانة ومحاسنها النيابة عن الله تعالى في إجابة المضطر لأنها لا تكون إلا المحتاج كالقرض فلذا كانت الصدقة بعشرة والقرض بثمانية عشر. وهي بالتشديد كأنها منسوبة إلى العار لأن طلبها عار وعيب؛ كذا في المصباح. وفي المغرب أنها منسوبة إلى العارة اسم من الإعارة وأخذها من العار العيب خطأ. النهاية أن ما في المغرب هو المعول عليه لأنه الله باشر الاستعارة فلو كان العار في طلبها لما باشرها ا هـ . وفي المبسوط : إنها مشتقة من التعاور وهو التناوب

قوله : (هي تمليك المنافع بغير عوض) وهذا تعريفها شرعاً وأشار به إلى الرد على الكرخي القائل بأنها إباحة وليست بتمليك، ويشهد لما في المتن الأحكام من انعقادها بلفظ التمليك وجواز أن يعبر ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل، ولو كان إباحة لما جاز لأن المباح له ليس له أن يبيح لغيره وإنما لا يفسد هذا التمليك الجهالة لكونها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة لعدم لزومها كذا قال الشارحون. والمراد بالجهالة جهالة المنافع المملكة لا جهالة العين المستعارة بدليل ما في الخلاصة : لو استعار من آخر حماراً فقال ذلك الرجل لي حماران في الإصطبل فخد أحدهما واذهب فأخذ أحدهما وذهب به يضمن إذا هلك، ولو قال له خذ أحدهما أيهما شئت لا يضمن ا هـ . وانعقادها بلفظ الإباحة لأنه استعير للتمليك وقد قالوا علف الدابة على المستعير مطلقة كانت أو موقتة، وكذا نفقة العبد أما كسوته فعلى المعير ؛ كذا في الخلاصة وحكمها كونها أمانة
Book of al-'Ariyah. It is the granting of ownership of usufruct without compensation. It is valid with 'I gave you on loan' and 'I fed you my land' and 'I granted you my garment'. Book of al-'Ariyah. And it is distinguished from wadi'ah because there is granting of ownership in it, though they share trust. Its benefits: representing Allah in responding to the needy because it is only for the needy like qard. Hence sadaqah is ten and qard is eighteen. It is with tashdid, as if attributed to 'ar (shame) because requesting it is shameful and a defect, as in al-Misbah. In al-Maghrib, it is attributed to 'arah, the noun from i'arah, and taking it from 'ar (shame) is an error. The conclusion is that what is in al-Maghrib is relied upon because Allah performed the act of borrowing, so if there were shame in requesting it, He would not have done it. In al-Mabsut: it is derived from ta'awur which means alternation. His statement: 'It is the granting of ownership of usufruct without compensation' is its legal definition. He points to refuting al-Karkhi who says it is ibaha and not tamlik. The rulings in the matn testify to it: its conclusion with the wording of tamlik and the permissibility of using a less common expression. If it were ibaha, it would not be permissible because the one to whom something is made permissible cannot permit it to another. Ignorance does not invalidate this tamlik because it does not lead to dispute since it is not binding, as the commentators said. What is meant by ignorance is ignorance of the usufructs being given ownership, not ignorance of the borrowed object itself, as evidence by what is in al-Khulasa: If someone borrows a donkey from another and the man says 'I have two donkeys in the stable; take one and go,' and he takes one and goes, he is liable if it perishes; but if he says 'Take whichever of the two you wish,' he is not liable. And it is concluded with the wording of ibaha because it is used metaphorically for tamlik. They said: the fodder of the animal is on the borrower, whether the loan is absolute or time-bound, and similarly the maintenance of the slave, but his clothing is on the lender, as in al-Khulasa. Its ruling is that it is a trust.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of al-'Ariyah (Loan for Use) in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The author begins by defining 'ariyah as tamlik al-manafi' bi-ghayr 'iwad — giving ownership of usufruct without compensation. This definition immediately establishes the Hanafi position that 'ariyah is a transfer of ownership (tamlik), not mere permission (ibaha) as al-Karkhi held. The commentary refutes al-Karkhi by noting that if it were ibaha, the borrower could not permit others to use the item, but in Hanafi law, the borrower can sub-lend. Further evidence: the contract is concluded with tamlik wording, and ignorance of the exact usufruct does not invalidate it because the contract is non-binding, preventing disputes. The author supports this with an example from al-Khulasa: if the lender specifies 'take one of my two donkeys' and the borrower chooses, he is liable only if the donkey perishes after specific identification; if given a choice without specification, he is not liable. The passage also discusses expenses: fodder and slave maintenance are on the borrower; clothing of a slave on the lender. The fundamental ruling is that the borrowed item is an amanah (trust) in the borrower's hands.

Key Terms
العارية (al-'āriyah): A contract granting ownership of usufruct without compensation, a trust.
تمليك المنفعة (tamlīk al-manfa'ah): Transferring ownership of the right to use an object without transferring ownership of the object itself.
أمانة (amānah): Something held in trust; the borrower is not liable for loss except by negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, what is 'ariyah?
A) A gift of the object
B) A loan of money
C) Ownership of usufruct without compensation
D) Permission to use without ownership

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'ariyah as tamlik al-manafi' is foundational for all subsequent rulings on liability and rights.

intermediate

Refuting al-Karkhi: 'Ariyah as Tamlik, Not Ibaha
Refutes al-Karkhi's ibaha view with evidence from rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi refutation of al-Karkhi's ibaha view, citing evidence from the contract's wording and the borrower's right to sub-lend.

Core Idea
If 'ariyah were ibaha, the borrower could not sub-lend; because he can, it must be tamlik.

Al-Karkhi, a respected Hanafi scholar, argued that 'ariyah is merely permission (ibaha), not a transfer of ownership. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refutes this by pointing to the actual rulings of 'ariyah: the contract is concluded with tamlik wording, the borrower can grant permission to others, and ignorance of the specific usufruct does not render it void.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Al-Karkhi held that 'ariyah is ibaha (mere permission). The majority Hanafi position (including the author) holds that it is tamlik (transfer of ownership of usufruct).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
2
Identify the first evidence: wording
The contract is valid with tamlik words like 'a'artuka' and 'at'amtu', showing it is a tamlik. If it were ibaha, using tamlik words would be linguistically inappropriate.
The author also notes that ibaha wording is used metaphorically, but the real nature is tamlik.
3
Identify the second evidence: sub-lending
The borrower can give the item to another person. This is only possible if the borrower owns the usufruct (tamlik). If it were ibaha, the borrower would have no right to permit others.
This is a strong practical argument.
4
Analyze the ignorance example
The text cites al-Khulasa: if the lender says 'take one of my two donkeys' and the borrower takes one, he is liable if it perishes; but if the lender leaves the choice to the borrower, he is not liable. Ignorance of the exact usufruct does not invalidate the contract because it is non-binding (ghayr lazim). This aligns with tamlik, not ibaha.
Under ibaha, such ignorance might cause voidness.
5
Conclude with the ruling
The borrowed item is an amanah (trust) in the borrower's hands. The borrower is not liable for loss unless negligent. This ruling is consistent with tamlik.
Expenses like fodder and slave maintenance are on the borrower; clothing of a slave is on the lender.

كتاب العارية

هي تمليك المنفعة بلا عوض وتصح باعرتك وأطعمتك أرضي ومنحتك ثوبي

كتاب العارية

وفي أخرها عن الوديعة لأن فيها تمليكاً وإن اشتركا في الأمانة ومحاسنها النيابة عن الله تعالى في إجابة المضطر لأنها لا تكون إلا المحتاج كالقرض فلذا كانت الصدقة بعشرة والقرض بثمانية عشر. وهي بالتشديد كأنها منسوبة إلى العار لأن طلبها عار وعيب؛ كذا في المصباح. وفي المغرب أنها منسوبة إلى العارة اسم من الإعارة وأخذها من العار العيب خطأ. النهاية أن ما في المغرب هو المعول عليه لأنه الله باشر الاستعارة فلو كان العار في طلبها لما باشرها ا هـ . وفي المبسوط : إنها مشتقة من التعاور وهو التناوب

قوله : (هي تمليك المنافع بغير عوض) وهذا تعريفها شرعاً وأشار به إلى الرد على الكرخي القائل بأنها إباحة وليست بتمليك، ويشهد لما في المتن الأحكام من انعقادها بلفظ التمليك وجواز أن يعبر ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل، ولو كان إباحة لما جاز لأن المباح له ليس له أن يبيح لغيره وإنما لا يفسد هذا التمليك الجهالة لكونها لا تفضي إلى المنازعة لعدم لزومها كذا قال الشارحون. والمراد بالجهالة جهالة المنافع المملكة لا جهالة العين المستعارة بدليل ما في الخلاصة : لو استعار من آخر حماراً فقال ذلك الرجل لي حماران في الإصطبل فخد أحدهما واذهب فأخذ أحدهما وذهب به يضمن إذا هلك، ولو قال له خذ أحدهما أيهما شئت لا يضمن ا هـ . وانعقادها بلفظ الإباحة لأنه استعير للتمليك وقد قالوا علف الدابة على المستعير مطلقة كانت أو موقتة، وكذا نفقة العبد أما كسوته فعلى المعير ؛ كذا في الخلاصة وحكمها كونها أمانة
Book of al-'Ariyah. It is the granting of ownership of usufruct without compensation. It is valid with 'I gave you on loan' and 'I fed you my land' and 'I granted you my garment'. Book of al-'Ariyah. And it is distinguished from wadi'ah because there is granting of ownership in it, though they share trust. Its benefits: representing Allah in responding to the needy because it is only for the needy like qard. Hence sadaqah is ten and qard is eighteen. It is with tashdid, as if attributed to 'ar (shame) because requesting it is shameful and a defect, as in al-Misbah. In al-Maghrib, it is attributed to 'arah, the noun from i'arah, and taking it from 'ar (shame) is an error. The conclusion is that what is in al-Maghrib is relied upon because Allah performed the act of borrowing, so if there were shame in requesting it, He would not have done it. In al-Mabsut: it is derived from ta'awur which means alternation. His statement: 'It is the granting of ownership of usufruct without compensation' is its legal definition. He points to refuting al-Karkhi who says it is ibaha and not tamlik. The rulings in the matn testify to it: its conclusion with the wording of tamlik and the permissibility of using a less common expression. If it were ibaha, it would not be permissible because the one to whom something is made permissible cannot permit it to another. Ignorance does not invalidate this tamlik because it does not lead to dispute since it is not binding, as the commentators said. What is meant by ignorance is ignorance of the usufructs being given ownership, not ignorance of the borrowed object itself, as evidence by what is in al-Khulasa: If someone borrows a donkey from another and the man says 'I have two donkeys in the stable; take one and go,' and he takes one and goes, he is liable if it perishes; but if he says 'Take whichever of the two you wish,' he is not liable. And it is concluded with the wording of ibaha because it is used metaphorically for tamlik. They said: the fodder of the animal is on the borrower, whether the loan is absolute or time-bound, and similarly the maintenance of the slave, but his clothing is on the lender, as in al-Khulasa. Its ruling is that it is a trust.

Valid Wordings and Conditions for 'Ariyah
Details explicit and metaphorical wordings and necessary conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid explicit and metaphorical wordings for 'ariyah and identify the essential conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
Explicit or metaphorical wordings suffice for 'ariyah; the object must be beneficial and no compensation permitted.

This lesson examines the wordings that establish a valid loan ('ariyah) in Hanafi fiqh. We will distinguish between explicit (ṣarīḥ) and metaphorical (majāz) expressions, and outline the conditions that must be met for 'ariyah to be valid, including the prohibition of stipulating compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling context
Understand that 'ariyah is a contract for the non-gratuitous use of an object's usufruct without compensation. The passage discusses valid wordings and conditions.
2
List the explicit wordings
Identify which wordings are explicit (ṣarīḥ) for 'ariyah, such as 'I gave you on loan' (a'tartuka) and 'I mounted you' (hamaltuka). These directly indicate the transfer of usufruct.
The author states that 'manah' (grant) and 'hamal' (mount) are explicit for 'ariyah unless hibah is intended.
3
Recognize metaphorical wordings
Understand that some expressions are metaphorical, like 'I fed you my land' (aṭ‘amtuka arḍī), which is used when 'feeding' cannot be taken literally; it means giving the usufruct of the land.
Metaphorical wordings require context but are valid.
4
Apply the essential conditions
The borrowed object must be capable of benefit (qābil li al-intifā‘), and the contract must be free from any stipulation of compensation. If compensation is stipulated, it becomes ijarah (rental).
These conditions are necessary for a valid 'ariyah.
5
Note the rule of revocation
The lender may revoke the 'ariyah at any time because it is not binding. If revocation causes clear harm to the borrower, the loan ends but the borrower may keep the object with payment of equivalent rent (ujrat al-mithl).
This is illustrated by Qadi Khan's example of a borrowed slave-girl for breastfeeding.

Its condition is that the borrowed object must be capable of benefit and free from condition of compensation in the loan, so if compensation is stipulated, it becomes ijarah; as in al-Muhit. Explicit. Metaphorically. His statement: 'It is valid with 'I gave you on loan' and 'I fed you my land'' because the first is literal and the second is explicit because when 'feeding' is added to something that is not eaten, it is intended metaphorically as what is utilized from it, because it is its place. His statement: 'And I granted you my garment and I mounted you on my riding animal' is also explicit, so it gives 'ariyah as well without stopping at intention, but if he intends hibah, it is hibah; 'I granted you' means 'I gave you'. His statement: 'And I made my slave serve you' because it is permission for service. His statement: 'And my house is for you for dwelling' means from the perspective of dwelling, because 'my house' is mubtada, 'for you' is its khabar, and 'dwelling' is tamyiz indicating the relationship to the addressee. His statement: 'And my house is for you for life as a dwelling' — it is said 'amara al-dar' meaning 'I gave it to you for the duration of your life'; 'umra is a noun from it, so its meaning becomes: I have made its dwelling for you for your lifetime. If he says to another: 'I have rented this house to you for a month without compensation', it is 'ariyah; if he does not say 'for a month', it is not, in Qadi Khan's Fatawa. His statement: 'The lender may revoke whenever he wishes' because it is not binding. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, gave it absolutely, so it includes cases where his revocation causes clear harm to the borrower; then the loan is invalidated and the object remains with the equivalent rent. Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: A man borrowed a slave-girl from another to breastfeed his son, and she breastfed him. When he said to him: She is a loan; likewise. This is not an offer like 'Buy this garment of mine', and it is not correct to derive it from the requirement of acceptance because taking the slave is an actual acceptance, so it would be wadi'ah. Ponder. His statement: 'And it is explicit also, so it gives 'ariyah without stopping at intention, etc.' In al-Kafi by al-Allamah al-Nasafi: His statement in al-Hidayah: 'And I granted you this garment and I mounted you on this riding animal, if he does not intend hibah, because they are for tamlik al-'ayn; and when he intends hibah, it is carried on tamlik al-manafi' as a metaphor' is problematic in several respects. First: his saying 'if he does not intend hibah' — he should have said 'if he does not intend both' as indicated by the daleel. It can be answered that the pronoun refers to what was mentioned, like the verse 'A middle course between that' [2:68]. Second: he made these two expressions literal for tamlik al-'ayn and metaphorical for tamlik al-manfa'ah. Then he mentioned in the Book of Hibah in explaining its wordings: 'And I mounted you on this riding animal' if he intends hibah by the mounting, and he reasoned that mounting is literally riding, so it is 'ariyah, but it can also be hibah. Third: since they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn, and the literal meaning is intended by the wording without intention, so when he does not intend hibah, it is not carried on tamlik al-manfa'ah but on hibah. In al-Mustasfa sharh al-Nafi': We say: It is possible that they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn and metaphorical for tamlik al-manfa'ah, and this is what the author of al-Hidayah inclined to in the Book of 'Ariyah, and the estimation would be 'if he does not intend hibah and intends 'ariyah' because if the literal meaning is not intended, the metaphorical is not resorted to except when intended. And it is possible that it is the opposite, and Fakhr al-Islam pointed to it in his Mabsut and the author of al-Hidayah in the Book of Hibah, and his saying 'if he does not intend hibah' is for emphasis, because the absolute speech is carried on 'ariyah, so the intent is not restriction. And it is possible that both meanings are literal for them, and one is preferred because it is the lesser of the two, so it is carried upon it for certainty. End quote from al-Kifayah clarifying. His statement: 'And if he says to another: I have rented this house to you for a month, etc.' Al-Ramli said: And in...
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on wordings that effect 'ariyah. The author explains that expressions like 'I gave you as 'ariyah' are explicit, while 'I fed you my land' is metaphorical because 'feeding' is figuratively used for utilizing the land. Similarly, 'I granted you my garment' and 'I mounted you on my riding animal' are explicit for 'ariyah unless the lender intends hibah (gift). The condition for a valid 'ariyah is that the borrowed object must be capable of benefit and that no compensation is stipulated; if compensation is stipulated, it becomes ijarah (rental). The borrower may revoke the loan at any time because it is not binding, even if revocation causes harm to the borrower — in such case the loan is invalidated and the object remains with an equivalent rent. The passage also includes an extensive discussion from al-Kafi regarding the wordings 'manah' (grant) and 'haml' (mounting) — whether they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn (gift of the object) or tamlik al-manafi' (loan). There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: In al-Hidayah's Book of 'Ariyah, they are considered metaphors for tamlik al-manafi'; in the Book of Hibah, they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn. The author resolves that both meanings are possible, but the preferred interpretation for 'ariyah is that when not intending hibah, the words are taken for 'ariyah. The passage ends with a note from al-Ramli about a detail regarding 'ijarah without compensation'.

Key Terms
صريح (ṣarīḥ): An explicit wording that directly indicates 'ariyah without need for intention.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage; a word used in a sense other than its original literal meaning, requiring context or intention.
إجارة (ijārah): A lease or rental contract with compensation; if compensation is stipulated in 'ariyah, it becomes ijarah.
استعارة (isti'ā'rah): The act of borrowing; the term used in the Qur'an for Allah's borrowing from believers metaphorically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid explicit wording for ‘ariyah?
A) I sold you
B) I gave you on loan
C) I married you
D) I pawned you

Key Takeaway
For a valid ‘ariyah, the wording must indicate a loan of usufruct, the object must be beneficial, and no compensation may be stipulated.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Manah' and 'Hamal' Wordings for 'Ariyah
Discusses the Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether 'manah' and 'hamal' are explicit for 'ariyah or hibah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding whether 'manah' and 'hamal' are literal for tamlik al-'ayn or tamlik al-manafi', and state the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The wordings 'I granted' and 'I mounted' can be either hibah or 'ariyah; the default in the loan chapter is 'ariyah unless hibah intended.

This lesson explores a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the wordings 'manah' (I granted) and 'hamal' (I mounted). While some Hanafi authorities treat them as literal for property transfer (hibah), others consider them metaphorical for benefit transfer ('ariyah). We will analyze the arguments and the preferred resolution.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Are the words 'manah' (I granted) and 'hamal' (I mounted) literal for tamlik al-'ayn (hibah) or tamlik al-manafi' ('ariyah)?
2
Identify the conflicting views
In al-Hidayah's Kitab al-'Ariyah, the author treats 'manah' and 'hamal' as explicit for 'ariyah unless hibah is intended. In Kitab al-Hibah, he treats them as literal for hibah. Fakhr al-Islam in al-Mabsut holds the opposite.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not between madhahib.
3
Examine the proofs
The literal meaning (haqiqah) of 'manah' and 'hamal' supports tamlik al-'ayn. However, the context of 'ariyah and the principle of adna al-amrayn (the lesser of the two obligations) supports treating them as 'ariyah when hibah is not intended.
The principle adna al-amrayn means the speech is carried on the lesser obligation to be certain.
4
Trace the resolution
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the view that these wordings are explicit for 'ariyah when not intending hibah, based on the principle of carrying on the lesser (adna al-amrayn). The statement 'if he does not intend hibah' is not restrictive but emphatic.
The preferred view is that in the absence of intention, the default is 'ariyah.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a person says 'I granted you my garment' without any explicit intention, according to the mufta bihi view, it is 'ariyah (loan) unless he intended hibah. If he intended hibah, it becomes a gift.
This has practical implications: the lender can revoke a loan but not a gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: 'If he says to another: Take my slave...' apparently it is derived from the requirement of offer, and his saying 'Take...' And 'I mounted you on my riding animal, and I made my slave serve you, and my house is for you to dwell in, and my house is for you for life as a dwelling.' Qadi Khan's Fatawa. Its condition is that the borrowed object must be capable of benefit and free from condition of compensation in the loan, so if compensation is stipulated, it becomes ijarah; as in al-Muhit. Explicit. Metaphorically. His statement: 'It is valid with 'I gave you on loan' and 'I fed you my land'' because the first is literal and the second is explicit because when 'feeding' is added to something that is not eaten, it is intended metaphorically as what is utilized from it, because it is its place. His statement: 'And I granted you my garment and I mounted you on my riding animal' is also explicit, so it gives 'ariyah as well without stopping at intention, but if he intends hibah, it is hibah; 'I granted you' means 'I gave you'. His statement: 'And I made my slave serve you' because it is permission for service. His statement: 'And my house is for you for dwelling' means from the perspective of dwelling, because 'my house' is mubtada, 'for you' is its khabar, and 'dwelling' is tamyiz indicating the relationship to the addressee. His statement: 'And my house is for you for life as a dwelling' — it is said 'amara al-dar' meaning 'I gave it to you for the duration of your life'; 'umra is a noun from it, so its meaning becomes: I have made its dwelling for you for your lifetime. If he says to another: 'I have rented this house to you for a month without compensation', it is 'ariyah; if he does not say 'for a month', it is not, in Qadi Khan's Fatawa. His statement: 'The lender may revoke whenever he wishes' because it is not binding. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, gave it absolutely, so it includes cases where his revocation causes clear harm to the borrower; then the loan is invalidated and the object remains with the equivalent rent. Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: A man borrowed a slave-girl from another to breastfeed his son, and she breastfed him. When he said to him: She is a loan; likewise. This is not an offer like 'Buy this garment of mine', and it is not correct to derive it from the requirement of acceptance because taking the slave is an actual acceptance, so it would be wadi'ah. Ponder. His statement: 'And it is explicit also, so it gives 'ariyah without stopping at intention, etc.' In al-Kafi by al-Allamah al-Nasafi: His statement in al-Hidayah: 'And I granted you this garment and I mounted you on this riding animal, if he does not intend hibah, because they are for tamlik al-'ayn; and when he intends hibah, it is carried on tamlik al-manafi' as a metaphor' is problematic in several respects. First: his saying 'if he does not intend hibah' — he should have said 'if he does not intend both' as indicated by the daleel. It can be answered that the pronoun refers to what was mentioned, like the verse 'A middle course between that' [2:68]. Second: he made these two expressions literal for tamlik al-'ayn and metaphorical for tamlik al-manfa'ah. Then he mentioned in the Book of Hibah in explaining its wordings: 'And I mounted you on this riding animal' if he intends hibah by the mounting, and he reasoned that mounting is literally riding, so it is 'ariyah, but it can also be hibah. Third: since they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn, and the literal meaning is intended by the wording without intention, so when he does not intend hibah, it is not carried on tamlik al-manfa'ah but on hibah. In al-Mustasfa sharh al-Nafi': We say: It is possible that they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn and metaphorical for tamlik al-manfa'ah, and this is what the author of al-Hidayah inclined to in the Book of 'Ariyah, and the estimation would be 'if he does not intend hibah and intends 'ariyah' because if the literal meaning is not intended, the metaphorical is not resorted to except when intended. And it is possible that it is the opposite, and Fakhr al-Islam pointed to it in his Mabsut and the author of al-Hidayah in the Book of Hibah, and his saying 'if he does not intend hibah' is for emphasis, because the absolute speech is carried on 'ariyah, so the intent is not restriction. And it is possible that both meanings are literal for them, and one is preferred because it is the lesser of the two, so it is carried upon it for certainty. End quote from al-Kifayah clarifying. His statement: 'And if he says to another: I have rented this house to you for a month, etc.' Al-Ramli said: And in...
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on wordings that effect 'ariyah. The author explains that expressions like 'I gave you as 'ariyah' are explicit, while 'I fed you my land' is metaphorical because 'feeding' is figuratively used for utilizing the land. Similarly, 'I granted you my garment' and 'I mounted you on my riding animal' are explicit for 'ariyah unless the lender intends hibah (gift). The condition for a valid 'ariyah is that the borrowed object must be capable of benefit and that no compensation is stipulated; if compensation is stipulated, it becomes ijarah (rental). The borrower may revoke the loan at any time because it is not binding, even if revocation causes harm to the borrower — in such case the loan is invalidated and the object remains with an equivalent rent. The passage also includes an extensive discussion from al-Kafi regarding the wordings 'manah' (grant) and 'haml' (mounting) — whether they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn (gift of the object) or tamlik al-manafi' (loan). There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: In al-Hidayah's Book of 'Ariyah, they are considered metaphors for tamlik al-manafi'; in the Book of Hibah, they are literal for tamlik al-'ayn. The author resolves that both meanings are possible, but the preferred interpretation for 'ariyah is that when not intending hibah, the words are taken for 'ariyah. The passage ends with a note from al-Ramli about a detail regarding 'ijarah without compensation'.

Key Terms
صريح (ṣarīḥ): An explicit wording that directly indicates 'ariyah without need for intention.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage; a word used in a sense other than its original literal meaning, requiring context or intention.
إجارة (ijārah): A lease or rental contract with compensation; if compensation is stipulated in 'ariyah, it becomes ijarah.
استعارة (isti'ā'rah): The act of borrowing; the term used in the Qur'an for Allah's borrowing from believers metaphorically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, if a person says 'I granted you my garment' without stating intention, what is the ruling?
A) It is a gift (hibah)
B) It is a loan ('ariyah)
C) It is invalid due to ambiguity
D) It is a sale

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a wording can indicate either hibah or 'ariyah, the default is 'ariyah because it imposes less obligation (adna al-amrayn).

General Rulings of Loan (ʿĀriyah)
States the basic rules of loan: reclaim anytime, no liability without misuse, no renting or pledging.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three core rulings of ʿāriyah and explain why each follows from its non-binding nature.

Core Idea
Loan is non-binding: the lender may reclaim anytime, and the borrower bears no liability without misuse.

This lesson covers the foundational principles of loan (ʿāriyah) in Hanafi fiqh. Understand that the contract is gratuitous and revocable, distinguishing it from hire or pledge. The matn presents succinct rulings that form the basis for more complex scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that ʿāriyah is a non-binding (ghayr lāzim) contract of gratuitous use. Confirm that the lender (muʿīr) gives permission to the borrower (mustaʿīr) to use an item for free.
Contrast with binding contracts like sale or hire.
2
Analyze the right of reclamation
The matn states 'yarjiʿu al-muʿīr matā shāʾa' – the lender may reclaim the item at any time. This is a consequence of the contract being non-binding.
No fixed term for loan unless agreed without a binding promise.
3
Examine liability and prohibitions
If the item perishes without misuse (tāʿaddī) or negligence, the borrower is not held liable (lam yaḍman). Additionally, the borrower cannot rent out or pledge the loaned item, similar to a deposit (wadīʿah).
Misuse includes using in a way not permitted by the lender or beyond the scope of the loan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العارية ويرجع المعير متى شاء ولو هلكت بلا تعد لم يضمن ولا تؤجر ولا ترهن كالوديعة فإن [؟] صار الصبي لا يأخذ إلا منها قال المعير أردد علي خادمي قال أبو يوسف: ليس له ذلك وله مثل أجر خادمه إلى أن تفطم الصبي. وكذا لو استعار من رجل فرساً ليغزو عليه فأعاره الفرس أربعة أشهر ثم لقيه بعد شهرين في بلاد المسلمين فأراد أخذ الفرس كان له ذلك، وإن لقيه في بلاد الشرك في موضع لا يقدر على الكراء والشراء كان للمستعير أن لا يدفعه إليه لأن هذا ضرر بين وعلى المستعير أجر مثل الفرس من الموضع الذي طلب صاحبه إلى أدنى المواضع الذي يجد فيه شراء أو كراء ا هـ
Book of Loan. The lender may reclaim whenever he wishes, and if it perishes without misuse, he is not compensated, and it is not rented or pledged like a deposit. Then if a child does not accept except from her, the lender said: 'Return my servant to me.' Abu Yusuf said: 'He does not have that; rather he is entitled to the equivalent of his servant's wages until the child is weaned.' Likewise, if a man borrowed a horse to wage war, and the lender gave the horse for four months, then met him after two months in Muslim lands and wanted to take the horse, he has that right. But if he met him in enemy territory where he cannot find hire or purchase, the borrower may not hand it over because that would be clear harm; and the borrower owes the equivalent hire of the horse from the place where the owner demanded it to the nearest place where he can find purchase or hire.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage from the matn states the foundational rulings of loan (ʿāriyah). The lender has the right to reclaim the loaned property at any time; this is a non-binding contract. If the item perishes without misuse (taʿaddī) or negligence, the borrower is not liable. The loaned item cannot be rented out or pledged by the borrower, just like a deposit (wadīʿah). The commentary then presents a scenario: if a woman borrowed a servant to nurse a child who refuses others, and later the lender demands the servant back, Abu Yusuf rules that the lender cannot take the servant until the child is weaned, but the borrower must pay wages equivalent to the servant's hire. Similarly, in the case of a borrowed horse for war, the lender can reclaim it if they meet in Muslim lands; but if in enemy territory where no alternative transport is available, the borrower may keep it until returning to a place where hire or purchase is possible, paying the hire. This illustrates the legal consideration of necessity (ḍarūrah).

Key Terms
عارية (ʿāriyah): A contract where a lender allows a borrower to use an item for free, non-binding.
معير (muʿīr): The lender who gives the item as a loan.
مستعير (mustaʿīr): The borrower who receives the item for use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a ruling of ʿāriyah according to the passage?
A) The lender may reclaim the item at any time
B) The borrower is liable for any loss regardless of cause
C) The borrower may not rent out the item
D) The borrower may not pledge the item

Key Takeaway
The lender's right to reclaim at any time and the borrower's non-liability without misuse define ʿāriyah as a non-binding, gratuitous contract.

Exceptions for Necessity in Loan (ʿĀriyah)
Presents exceptions to the general rule based on necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Yusuf's exception regarding necessity to situations where reclaiming a loaned item causes harm.

Core Idea
Necessity can override the lender's right to reclaim, but the borrower must pay compensation.

This lesson examines two exceptions to the rule that a lender may reclaim anytime: a borrowed servant for nursing and a borrowed horse in enemy territory. Learn how necessity and harm modify the ruling. The passage presents these as fatwa from Abu Yusuf and as legal reasoning based on the principle of preventing harm (ḍarar).

Guided Path
1
Understand the servant case
A woman borrows a servant to nurse her child. The child refuses all other nurses. The lender demands the servant back. Abu Yusuf rules the lender cannot take the servant until weaning, but the borrower must pay wages.
The harm to the child (potential suffering or death) justifies the restriction.
2
Analyze the horse case
A man borrows a horse for war. The lender meets him in enemy territory after two months. If the borrower cannot hire or buy another animal, he may keep the horse until reaching a place where alternatives exist, paying hire for the extra use.
The harm of being stranded in enemy territory outweighs the lender's immediate right to reclaim.
3
Identify the common principle
Both exceptions arise from dire necessity (ḍarūrah) that would cause clear harm (ḍarar bayyin) to the borrower or a third party. Compensation is required to balance the lender's loss.
The borrower must pay the equivalent hire (ujrat al-mithl) for the extended use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Takeaway
