Detailed Conditions for Liability in Loan (ʿĀriyah)
Expands on when the borrower is liable for destruction due to misuse (taʿaddī).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a borrower is liable for destruction of a loaned item, identify specific acts that constitute misuse (taʿaddī), and apply the principle that deviation to an equivalent or better use does not trigger liability.

Core Idea
No liability without misuse; misuse is defined by custom and purpose.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the key condition for liability in loans: misuse (taʿaddī). It clarifies that without misuse, the borrower is not liable even if the item perishes, and provides numerous examples of what constitutes misuse. Additionally, it addresses special cases such as items belonging to another, who may lend, and the nuance that a deviation to an equivalent or better use does not create liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline rule
The passage begins by stating that if the loaned item perishes without misuse (bila taʿaddī), the borrower is not liable. This is the default rule.
This applies even if a condition of liability was stipulated – such a condition is invalid, like in a pledge.
2
Understand the mustaḥaqq case
If the loaned item turns out to belong to a third party (mustaḥaqq), the borrower must compensate the true owner, but has no recourse against the lender. The true owner may also hold the lender liable, but then the lender cannot claim from the borrower.
This differs from the depositee (mūdiʿ) who can recourse against the depositor if he pays the true owner.
3
Note who may lend
The passage specifies: a father cannot lend his minor child's property; an authorized slave may lend; a wife lending household items from her husband's property normally incurs no liability, but for large animals like horses or oxen, both she and the borrower are liable.
The ruling is based on custom: what women usually handle is exempt from liability.
4
Examine examples of misuse (taʿaddī)
Multiple acts are listed as misuse: harsh curb, poking an eye, overloading, overworking, leaving in a dangerous place, using for a different purpose or location, coupling with a stronger animal without custom, and sleeping while lying down in the desert (if sitting, not liable except in travel).
Custom plays a key role: e.g., leaving to graze is not misuse if customary; otherwise it is.
5
Recognize the exception for equivalent deviation
The passage ends with a qualifier from Jamiʿ al-Fusulayn: if the borrower deviates to an equivalent or lesser use (e.g., plowing an equivalent field, carrying similar weight), he is not liable.
This shows that liability for misuse is not triggered by any deviation, only by a change that increases risk or violates the lender's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو هلكت بلا تعد لا يضمن أطلقه فشمل ما إذا هلكت في حال الاستعمال وما إذا شرط عليه الضمان فإنه شرط باطل كشرط عدم الضمان في الرهن إذا هلك ؛ كذا في المحيط. وهذا إذا لم يتبين أنها مستحقة للغير، فإن ظهر استحقاقها أنها للغير ضمنها ولا رجوع له على المعير لأنه متبرع وللمستحق أن يضمن المعير، وإذا ضمنه لا رجوع له على المستعير بخلاف المودع إذا ضمنها للمستحق حيث يرجع على المودع لأنه عامل له ولا يملك والد الصغير إعارة مال ولده، والعبد المأذون يملك أن يعير والمرأة إذا أعارت شيئاً من ملك الزوج فهلك إن كان شيئاً داخل البيت وما يكون في أيديهن عادة فلا ضمان على أحد، أما في الفرس أو الثور فيضمن المستعير والمرأة؛ كذا في النهاية قيد بقوله بلا تعد لأنه لو تعدى ضمنها كما لو كبحها باللجام أو فقأ عينها بالضرب أو حملها ما يعلم أن مثلها لا يحمله أو استعملها ليلاً ونهاراً مما لا يستعمل مثلها في الدواب وكذا لو نزل عن الدابة ودخل المسجد وتركها في السكة فهلكت يضمن على الأصح وكذا إذا استعار دابة ليركبها في حاجته إلى ناحية مسماة فأخرجها إلى النهر ليسقيها وهي غير تلك الناحية ضمن إذا هلكت وكذا إذا استعار ثوراً ليكرب به أرضه فكرب أرضاً أخرى يضمن إذا عطب، وكذا إذا قرنه بثور أعلى منه ولم تجر العادة به فهلك وكذا إذا نام في المفازة ومقود الدابة في يده فسرقت إن كان مضطجعاً، وإن كان جالساً لا يضمن في غير السفر، وإن كان في السفر لا يضمن، سواء نام قاعداً أو مضطجعاً إذا كان المستعار تحت رأسه أو موضوعاً بين يديه أو حواليه بحيث يعد حافظاً عادة . ولو تركه في المرج يرعى إن كانت العادة هكذا لا يضمن، وإن لم يعلم أو كانت العادة مشتركة يضمن. ولو جعله في القربة وليس للقربة باب مفتوح لا يضمن . قوله : (فكرب أرضاً أخرى قال في جامع الفصولين أقول: ينبغي أن لا يضمن لو كرب مثل المعينة أو أرخى منها كما لو استعار دابة للحمل وسمى نوعاً فخالف لا يضمن لو حمل مثل المسمى
His saying: (And if it perishes without misuse, he is not liable) is absolute, and includes when it perishes during use and when he stipulates liability – for that condition is invalid, like the condition of non-liability in a pledge when it perishes; thus in al-Muhit. And this is when it is not revealed that the item belongs to another. If its entitlement appears that it belonged to another, the borrower guarantees it and has no recourse against the lender because he is a benefactor; the true owner may hold the lender liable. If the lender pays, he has no recourse against the borrower, unlike the depositee who when he pays the true owner, he can recourse against the depositor because he acted for him. And the father of a minor does not have the right to lend his child's property; the authorized slave may lend; and if a woman lends something from her husband's property and it perishes, if it is something inside the house that women usually handle, there is no liability; but for a horse or ox, the borrower and the woman are liable. Thus in al-Nihayah. He restricted with 'without misuse' because if he misuses, he is liable. For example, if he curb it with the bridle harshly, or pokes its eye by hitting, or loads it with what it cannot normally carry, or uses it night and day as is not normal for such animals. Likewise, if he dismounts and enters the mosque leaving the animal in the road and it perishes, he is liable according to the soundest opinion. Likewise, if he borrows a beast to ride to a specified direction but takes it to the river to water it (which is not that direction), he is liable if it perishes. Likewise, if he borrows an ox to plow his field but plows another field, he is liable if it perishes. Likewise, if he couples it with a stronger ox without custom, and it perishes. Likewise, if he sleeps in the desert with the reins in his hand and it is stolen, if he was lying down he is liable; if he was sitting, not liable except in travel? Actually: in travel, not liable whether sitting or lying if the borrowed item is under his head or placed before him such that he is considered a caretaker by custom. If he leaves it to graze in the meadow if that is customary, he is not liable; if not known or if the custom varies, he is liable. If he puts it in a waterskin and the waterskin has no open opening, he is not liable. His saying: (and plowed another field) – he said in Jamiʿ al-Fusulayn: I say it should not be liable if he plowed like the specified field or less, just as if he borrows a beast to carry a specified type and he carries something else but of equal weight, he is not liable.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the phrase 'without misuse' from the matn. It first clarifies that the ruling of no liability covers two situations: when the item perishes during normal use, and when a condition of liability was stipulated (which is invalid). Then it discusses the case where the loaned item turns out to belong to another (mustaḥaqq): the borrower is liable to the true owner and has no recourse against the lender; the true owner may also hold the lender liable, but then the lender cannot recourse against the borrower, unlike the depositee (mūdiʿ) who can recourse against the depositor. Next, it addresses who may lend: a father cannot lend his minor child's property; an authorized slave may lend; a wife lending something from her husband's property: if it is household items normally in their hands, no liability, but for animals like horses or oxen, both the borrower and the wife are liable. The core of the passage lists many examples of misuse (taʿaddī) that trigger liability: harsh curb, poking eye, overloading, overworking, leaving in a dangerous place, using for a different purpose or place, coupling with a stronger animal without custom, sleeping in a desert while lying down (if sitting, not liable unless in travel? Actually the text says for travel no liability), leaving to graze against custom, etc. Finally, it qualifies that if the borrower deviates to something equal or better (like plowing an equivalent field or carrying similar weight), he should not be liable, as per Jamiʿ al-Fusulayn.

Key Terms
تعدي (taʿaddī): Misuse or exceeding the limits of proper use of the loaned item, leading to liability.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or destruction of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a borrowed ox perishes while plowing a different field, which of the following is true?
A) The borrower is liable only if the ox was overworked.
B) The borrower is not liable if the second field is of the same type.
C) The borrower is liable because plowing another field is misuse.
D) The borrower is liable only if the lender forbade plowing other fields.

Key Takeaway
A borrower is liable for destruction only if he commits an act of misuse (taʿaddī) beyond customary use, but deviation to an equivalent or better use does not create liability.

intermediate
15 min
Borrower's Right to Lend and Restrictions by Time or Purpose
Discussion of borrower's sub-loaning rights, restrictions, and liability for deviation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a borrower may sub-loan a borrowed item, identify the restrictions that must be followed, and apply the ruling on liability for deviation or renting out.

Core Idea
A borrower may sub-loan only for generic uses; for personal uses, sub-lending may exhaust permission and trigger liability.

When you borrow something, you generally have the right to use it, but can you let someone else use it? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the nature of the use and any restrictions placed by the lender. This lesson clarifies the rules of sub-loaning (i'arah) and what happens if you deviate from the terms or rent out the item.

Guided Path
1
Classify the intended use
Determine if the use varies by person (e.g., riding, wearing) or is generic (carrying, dwelling). Only generic uses allow sub-loaning without restriction.
If the loan is unrestricted for a personal use, sub-loaning is still permissible but may exhaust permission.
2
Check for restrictions
If the loan is restricted by time, purpose, or both, the borrower must adhere exactly. If unrestricted, the borrower may use any type at any time.
Restrictions can be explicit (e.g., 'for one day') or implicit (e.g., 'to carry wheat').
3
Evaluate deviation
If the borrower deviates from the terms, determine whether the deviation is to a worse condition (liable), equal (no liability), or better (no liability unless more burdensome).
Deviation to equal (e.g., same weight of different grain) often does not trigger liability, but check physical burden (e.g., barley takes more space).
4
Assess liability for sub-loaning and renting
Renting out makes the borrower a usurper (ghasib) and liable. Sub-loaning generic uses is allowed; sub-loaning personal uses may lead to dispute if borrower later uses it himself.
The relied-upon view (Bazdawi) holds the borrower liable if he rides after letting another ride an unrestricted loan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجر فعطبت ضمن ويعير ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل فلو قيدها بوقت أو منفعة أو بهما لا إن نام مضطجعاً أو قاعداً. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان لو استعار دابة للذهاب فأمسكها في بيته فهلكت كان ضامناً لأنه أعارها للذهاب لا للإمساك . في البيت . قوله : (ولا تؤجر لأن الإجارة أقوى لأنها لازمة فلو ملكها لزم لزوم ما لا يلزم وهو العارية أو عدم لزوم ما يلزم وهو الإجارة قوله : (ولا) ترهن كالوديعة) لأن الرهن إيفاء وليس له أن يوفي دينه بمال غيره بغير إذنه وله أن يودع على المفتى به وهو المختار، وصحح بعضهم عدمه ويتفرع عليه ما لو أرسلها على يد أجنبي فهلكت يضمن على الثاني لا الأول وسيأتي قريباً قوله : (فإن أجر فعطبت ضمن لأنه متعد بالتسليم فصار غاصباً، وله أن يضمن المستأجر كالمستأجر من الغاصب وإذا ضمنه رجع على المستعير إذا لم يعلم أنه كان عارية في يده بخلاف ما إذا علم وبخلاف المستعير إذا ضمن ليس له الرجوع على المستأجر لأنه بالضمان تبين أنه آجر ملك نفسه ويتصدق بالأجرة عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف؛ كذا في الخلاصة. قوله : (ويعير ما لا يختلف بالمستعمل) لكونه ملك المنفعة فملك أن يملكها. قيد بما لا يختلف وهو الحمل والاستخدام والسكنى لأن ما يختلف ليس له فيه أن يعير كاللبس والركوب لكن بشرط أن تكون مقيدة، أما لو كانت مطلقة كما لو استعار دابة للركوب أو ثوباً للبس له أن : رهما ويكون ذلك تعييناً للراكب ،واللابس فإن ركب هو بعد ذلك قال يعير الإمام علي البزدوي يكون ضامناً. وقال السرخسي وخواهر زاده : لا يضمن؛ كذا في فتاوی قاضيخان وصحح الأول في الكافي قوله : (فلو قيدها بوقت أو منفعة أو بهما لا يتجاوز عما سواه وأن أطلق له أن ينتفع أي نوع شاء في أي وقت شاء) يعني أنها على أربعة أوجه لأن الإطلاق والتقييد دائر بين شيئين : الوقت والانتفاع وأشار بقوله «لا يتجاوز» إلى أنه لا يتعدى المسمى فأفاد أنه لا بد أن تكون المخالفة إلى شر، فلو خالف إلى مثل المسمى بأن استعار دابة ليحمل عليها عشرة أقفزة من حنطة معينة فحمل عليها هذا القدر من حنطة أخرى أو ليحمل عليها حنطة نفسه فحمل عليها حنطة غيره أو خالف إلى خير من المسمي بأن حمل هذا القدر من الشعير لا يكون ضامناً لأنه إنما يعتبر من تقييده ما يكون مفيداً حتى لو سمى مقداراً . الحنطة وزناً فحمل مثل ذلك الوزن من الشعير يضمن لأنه يأخذ من ظهر الدابة أكثر مما تأخذه الحنطة؛ كذا في النهاية. وصحح الولوالجي عدم الضمان. وفي المحيط : إذا استعار دابة ليركبها فركبها وأركب غيره فعطبت ضمن نصف قيمتها اهـ. وإذا قيدها بوقت فهي مطلقة إلا في حق الوقت حتى لو لم يردها بعد مضي الوقت مع الإمكان ضمن إذا هلكت وكذا إذا قرنه بثور أعلى منه في جامع الفصولين ما يفيد أن أغلى بالعين المعجمة حيث قال : استعار ثوراً قيمته خمسون ليستعمله فقرنه مع ثور قيمته مائة يبرأ لو كان الناس يفعلون مثل ذلك وإلا ضمن.
If he rented it out and it perished, he is liable. And he may lend what does not vary by use. If he restricts it by time or purpose or both, then he may not exceed. If he sleeps lying down or sitting. In Fatawa Qadikhan: if he borrowed a beast to go and then kept it in his house and it perished, he is liable because it was lent for going, not for keeping in the house. His saying: (And it is not rented out because renting is stronger since it is binding; if he rented it out, it would bind what is not binding (loan) or not bind what is binding (rent). His saying: (And not pledged like a deposit) because pledge is fulfillment; he has no right to fulfill his debt with another's property without permission. He may deposit it according to the mufta bihi and that is the chosen view. Some corrected to prohibition, and from this branches: if he sends it with a stranger and it perishes, he is liable according to the second view, not the first. It will come soon. His saying: (If he rents it out and it perishes, he is liable because he exceeded by handing it over, becoming a usurper. He may hold the lessee liable like the lessee from a usurper. If the lessee pays, he may recourse against the borrower if the lessee did not know it was a loan in his hand; otherwise not. And unlike the borrower if he pays, he has no recourse against the lessee because by the payment it becomes clear that he rented his own property, and he gives the rent in charity according to both, contrary to Abu Yusuf; thus in al-Khulasa. His saying: (And he may lend what does not vary by use) because he owns the usufruct so he owns making others own it. Restricted to what does not vary, which is carrying, employing, and dwelling, because what varies like wearing and riding he cannot lend – but only if restricted. As for unrestricted, like if he borrows a beast to ride or a garment to wear, he may let another use it, and that becomes a specification for the rider or wearer. If he himself rides later, according to Imam Ali al-Bazdawi he is liable. Sarakhsi and Khwarizadeh said: not liable; thus in Fatawa Qadikhan. The first is corrected in al-Kafi. His saying: (If he restricts it by time or purpose or both, he may not exceed what is specified; and if unrestricted, he may use any type at any time) means there are four aspects because restriction and release circle between two things: time and benefit. By saying 'he may not exceed', it indicates that he does not exceed the specified. So he says that the violation must be to a worse condition. If he deviates to an equal like borrowing a beast to carry ten qafizes of specified wheat but carries the same amount of other wheat, or carries other's wheat instead of his own, or deviates to better like carrying barley of the same amount, he is not liable because only beneficial restrictions matter. Even if he specified wheat by weight, and carries the same weight of barley, he is liable because barley takes up more space. Thus in al-Nihaya. Al-Walwaliji corrected that there is no liability. In al-Muhit: if he borrows a beast to ride, then rides and lets another ride, and it perishes, he is liable for half its value. And if he restricts by time, it is unrestricted except as to time; so if he does not return it after the time has passed with possibility, he is liable if it perishes. Likewise, if he couples it with a stronger ox as in Jami' al-Fusulayn, it indicates that if he uses it with a more valuable ox, he is free if people do that; otherwise liable.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage addresses three main issues regarding loan: (1) The borrower cannot rent or pledge the loaned item, because renting is a binding contract and would impose a binding obligation on a non-binding loan; pledging would involve using another's property to secure a debt without permission. (2) The borrower may lend (sub-loan) the item to others only if the use does not vary (e.g., carrying, employing, dwelling – which are generic). For uses that vary by person like riding or wearing, the borrower cannot sub-lend unless the loan was unrestricted. If unrestricted, the borrower may let another use it, but if the borrower himself then uses it, there is a dispute: Imam Ali al-Bazdawi holds him liable because he exceeded his right; Sarakhsi and Khwarizadeh do not. The relied upon view is al-Bazdawi's. (3) If the loan is restricted by time or purpose, the borrower must adhere. Deviation to a worse condition (e.g., different destination, extra weight) triggers liability. Deviation to an equal or better condition (same weight of different grain, plowing an equivalent field) does not cause liability, unless the substance is more burdensome (like barley taking more space). If the borrower rents out the loaned item and it perishes, he is liable as a usurper; he may then hold the lessee liable if the lessee did not know it was a loan. The borrower cannot recourse against the lessee if he pays the owner; he must give the rental fee in charity. Finally, if the loan is time-restricted, after the time expires the borrower becomes liable if he does not return it promptly.

Key Terms
يختلف بالمستعمل (yakhtalifu bil-mustaʿmal): The usage that varies depending on the person, like riding (different riders have different styles) and wearing (different sizes/fit).
غصب (ghaṣb): Usurpation; unlawfully taking possession of another's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a borrower borrows a horse without restriction, then lets his friend ride it, and later the borrower rides it himself and the horse perishes, what is the dispute?
A) All agree he is not liable
B) Bazdawi says liable, Sarakhsi says not
C) Abu Yusuf says liable, Muhammad says not
D) He is always liable because of misuse

Key Takeaway
Sub-loaning is permissible only for generic uses; deviation from restrictions may trigger liability, and the mufta bihi holds the borrower liable if he uses the item after sub-loaning an unrestricted personal-use loan.
